المبحث السادس
تلامذته والآخذون عنه

لا شك أن للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني خلال هذا العمر الطويل في نشر العلم والتعليم عدداً كبيراً من التلاميذ، حضروا دروسه، وانتفعوا بعلومه، وأخذوا عنه، لكن لم يهتم المترجمون بذكر أسمائهم مجتمعين، وممن يسر الله لي الوقوف عليه منهم: 
١- العلامة الشيخ طاهر بن صالح بن أحمد الجزائري الدمشقي صاحب المؤلفات المُتقنة المحرّرة، والعلوم المتنوعة، المولود بدمشق سنة ١٢٦٨هـ، والمتوفى بها سنة ١٣٣٨هـ، وكان قد هاجر والده إلى دمشق سنة ١٢٦٣هـ.
٢- العلامة الشيخ محمد عطا الله بن إبراهيم الكسم، الفقيه الحنفي، مفتي دمشق، المولود سنة ١٢٦٠هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٥٧هـ، وقد ذكر مترجموه أنه كان يحضر عند الشيخ الميداني درسين كل أسبوع. 
٣- ولده الشيخ إسماعيل بن عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، المولود سنة ١٢٥٤هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢هـ، فقد قرأ على والده، واستفاد منه.
٤- العلامة المقرئ الشيخ عبد الغني بن حسن بن إبراهيم البيطار، المولود سنة ١٢٤٠هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٥هـ.
٥- العلامة الفقيه الشيخ محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، أمين الفتوى بدمشق، المولود سنة ١٢٣١هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٢هـ. وقد جاء ذكر تلمذته عليه في آخر نسخة مخطوطة من كتاب الميداني: «إسعاف المريدين»، محفوظة في الظاهرية بدمشق، برقم (٤٧٩٣)، وفي آخرها: تم نسخها على يد الحقير الذليل الجاني المحتار، والراجي عفو ورضا الجليل المسامح الغفار: محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، وفقه مولاه لما يختار، تلميذ مؤلفها المحفوظ، وذلك قبيل طلوع فجر الاثنين ثاني يوم ذي الحجة.
The Sixth Section: His Students and Those Who Took from Him

There is no doubt that Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, during this long life in spreading knowledge and education, had a large number of students: they attended his lessons, benefited from his sciences, and took from him. However, the biographers did not bother to mention their names collectively. Among those whom Allah facilitated for me to find are:
1- The scholar, Shaykh Tahir ibn Salih ibn Ahmad al-Jazairi al-Dimashqi, author of precise and well-edited works and diverse sciences, born in Damascus in 1268 AH, and died there in 1338 AH. His father had migrated to Damascus in 1263 AH.
2- The scholar, Shaykh Muhammad Ata Allah ibn Ibrahim al-Kasm, the Hanafi jurist, Mufti of Damascus, born in 1260 AH, and died in 1357 AH. His biographers mention that he used to attend two lessons per week with Shaykh al-Maydani.
3- His son, Shaykh Ismail ibn Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, born in 1254 AH, and died in 1332 AH. He read under his father and benefited from him.
4- The scholar and reciter, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani ibn Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar, born in 1240 AH, and died in 1315 AH.
5- The scholar and jurist, Shaykh Muhammad ibn Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar, Amin al-Fatwa in Damascus, born in 1231 AH, and died in 1312 AH. His studentship with him is mentioned at the end of a manuscript copy of al-Maydani's book 'Is'af al-Muridin', preserved in al-Zahiriyya in Damascus (number 4793), at the end of which: It was copied by the humble, lowly, sinful, and chooser, hoping for the pardon and pleasure of the Majestic, All-Pardoning, All-Forgiving: Muhammad ibn Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar, may Allah guide him to what He chooses, the student of its protected author, just before dawn on Monday, the second day of Dhu al-Hijjah.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of five of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's prominent students. The author notes that although many students studied under Shaykh al-Maydani, biographers did not collect their names; he then lists those he was able to document. The first is Tahir al-Jazairi, a prolific author. The second is Muhammad Ata Allah al-Kasm, a Hanafi jurist and Mufti of Damascus, who attended two weekly lessons with al-Maydani. Third is the Shaykh's own son, Ismail, who read under his father. Fourth is Abd al-Ghani al-Bitar, a scholar of Qur'anic recitation. Fifth is Muhammad al-Bitar, who served as Amin al-Fatwa (official issuer of fatwas) in Damascus; his connection to al-Maydani is confirmed in a manuscript of al-Maydani's work 'Is'af al-Muridin'. The passage provides biographical details and manuscript evidence, illustrating the transmission of Hanafi knowledge in Damascus.

Key Terms
التلامذة (al-talamidha): Students; those who attend a teacher's lessons and acquire knowledge from him.
المفتي (al-mufti): The official jurisconsult who issues fatwas (legal opinions) based on the Hanafi school.
أمين الفتوى (Amin al-fatwa): The trustee or official responsible for issuing fatwas; a high-ranking position in the judicial system of Damascus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Shaykh Muhammad Ata Allah al-Kasm
C) Shaykh Ismail al-Maydani
D) Shaykh Muhammad al-Bitar

Key Takeaway
The transmission of Hanafi knowledge relies on documented teacher-student relationships, as exemplified by the students of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.

Life of the Author

The Scholarly Network of al-Maidani: His Students and Transmitters
Biographical listing of six students/transmitters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six students/transmitters of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and state their roles in preserving and transmitting Hanafi fiqh knowledge.

Core Idea
Biographical chains (isnad) preserve the authority of fiqh texts; knowing the transmitters strengthens trust in transmitted rulings.

This lesson introduces you to the scholarly circle of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, the commentator of Al-Quduri. You will meet six key figures who studied under him, copied his works, or transmitted his teachings. Understanding these biographical links is essential for appreciating the chain of authority (sanad) in Hanafi scholarship. The passage also gives insight into the immense dedication of scholars like Muhammad al-Bitar, who copied five thousand quires by hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Maidani's son
Note the name, birth and death years, and relationship to the author. He studied directly under his father.
Isma'il ibn Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maidani (1254-1332 AH).
2
Identify the two al-Bitar scholars
First: Abd al-Ghani al-Bitar, a Qur'an reciter (muqri'). Second: Muhammad al-Bitar, a faqih and official mufti of Damascus. Note the manuscript evidence showing Muhammad copied al-Maidani's work.
Muhammad al-Bitar's copying activity is remarkable: five thousand quires.
3
Examine the manuscript evidence
The copyist's note at the end of 'Is‘af al-Muridin' provides a direct link of study and transmission. It also shows the date and circumstance of copying.
The manuscript number is (4793) in al-Zahiriyya, Damascus.
4
Identify the remaining three scholars
Mustafa Kamal al-Sharif (Damascus), Habib al-Rahman al-Husayni (India/Medina), and Ali ibn Zahir al-Watri (Medina, hadith specialist).
They represent the geographic spread of al-Maidani's influence.
5
Reflect on the significance of copying
Manual copying (نسخ) was a primary method of preserving and transmitting texts. The quantity copied by Muhammad al-Bitar shows extraordinary dedication.
Each quire is three leaves; five thousand quires is approximately 15,000 pages.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

ولده الشيخ إسماعيل بن عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، المولود سنة ١٢٥٤هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢ هـ ، فقد قرأ على والده، واستفاد منه

٤- العلامة المقرئ الشيخ عبد الغني بـن حـسـن بـن إبراهيم البيطار، المولود سنة ١٢٤٠هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٥هـ

٥- العلامة الفقيه الشيخ محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، أمين الفتوى بدمشق، المولود سنة ۱۲۳۱هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٢هـ . وقد جاء ذكر تلمذته عليه في آخر نسخة مخطوطة من كتـاب الميداني: «إسعاف المريدين، محفوظة في الظاهرية بدمشق، برقم (٤٧٩٣)، وفي آخرها : تم نسخها على يد الحقـيـر الـذليـل الجـاني المحتار، والراجي عفو ورضا الجليل المسامح الغفار: محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، وفقه مولاه لما يختار، تلميذ مؤلفهـا المحفوظ، وذلك قبيل طلوع فجر الاثنين ثـانـي يـوم ذي الحجة الحرام، سنة إحدى وستين ومائتين وألف، أسعده الله آمین». اهـ

وبمناسبة نسخه لهذه الرسالة، فقد ذكروا في ترجمته «أنه لازم نسخ الكتب فوق العادة، وأنه نَسَخ في زمنه خمسة آلاف كـراس وزيادة». اهـ، «والكراس ثلاث ورقات، وهو قدر كبير جداً يتعجب منه، لكنه عون الله وتوفيقه.

٦- العلامة الشيخ مصطفى كمال بن محمد الشريف، المولود بدمشق سنة ١٢٦٣هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٧هـ، وله مؤلفات عديدة.

٧- الشيخ العارف بالله حبيب الرحمن الحسيني الهندي المدني، من علماء أوائل القرن الرابع عشر الهجري.

٨- العلامة المحدث الشيخ علي بن ظـاهـر الـوتري المدني، المولود في المدينة المنورة سنة ١٢٦١هـ ، والمتوفى بها سنة ١٣٢٢هـ
Chapter One: Biography of the Allama Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani

His son, Shaykh Isma'il ibn Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maidani, born in 1254 AH and died in 1332 AH, studied under his father and benefited from him.

4- The Allama Qur'an reciter Shaykh Abd al-Ghani ibn Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar, born in 1240 AH and died in 1315 AH.

5- The Allama jurist Shaykh Muhammad ibn Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar, the mufti of Damascus, born in 1231 AH and died in 1312 AH. Mention of his studying under al-Maidani appears at the end of a manuscript of al-Maidani's book 'Is‘af al-Muridin', preserved in al-Zahiriyya in Damascus, number (4793), at the end of which: 'It was copied by the humble, lowly, sinful, chosen one, hoping for the pardon and pleasure of the Majestic, the Forgiver: Muhammad ibn Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar, may Allah guide him to what He chooses, a student of its preserved author, shortly before dawn on Monday the second day of Dhu al-Hijjah al-Haram, in the year 1261 AH, may Allah grant him success. Amin.'

And on the occasion of his copying this treatise, they mentioned in his biography: 'He was excessively devoted to copying books beyond the norm, and he copied in his time five thousand quires and more.' A quire is three leaves, and it is a very large amount that is amazing, but it is by Allah's help and grace.

6- The Allama Shaykh Mustafa Kamal ibn Muhammad al-Sharif, born in Damascus in 1263 AH and died in 1317 AH, and he has numerous works.

7- The gnostic saint Habib al-Rahman al-Husayni al-Hindi al-Madani, from the scholars of the early fourteenth century AH.

8- The Allama hadith specialist Shaykh Ali ibn Zahir al-Watri al-Madani, born in Medina in 1261 AH and died there in 1323 AH.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri by Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. The author lists several of his prominent students and associates. The first is his own son, Shaykh Isma'il, who studied directly under him. Then he mentions two members of the al-Bitar family: Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Bitar, a renowned Qur'an reciter, and his son Shaykh Muhammad al-Bitar, who served as mufti of Damascus. The note about the manuscript of 'Is‘af al-Muridin' provides evidence of the student-teacher relationship and shows the practice of copying books for transmission. The extraordinary copying activity of Shaykh Muhammad al-Bitar—five thousand quires, each quire being three leaves—demonstrates the immense dedication to preserving Islamic knowledge. Then follows mention of Shaykh Mustafa Kamal al-Sharif, a scholar with many works, and two scholars from Medina: Shaykh Habib al-Rahman al-Husayni al-Hindi and Shaykh Ali ibn Zahir al-Watri al-Madani, a hadith specialist. The passage highlights the wide scholarly network radiating from al-Maidani, encompassing Damascus, Medina, and India.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-‘Allāmah): A title of high scholarly distinction, meaning 'the most learned'.
المقرئ (al-Muqri’): A specialist in the variant readings (qirā’āt) of the Qur’an.
الفقيه (al-Faqīh): A jurist well-versed in Islamic law (fiqh), especially one capable of issuing fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Understanding the transmitters of a fiqh text is essential for assessing its authenticity and authority in the Hanafi tradition.

The Scholarly Network of Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical listing of scholars connected to al-Maydani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical entries in al-Maydani's scholarly network and explain the importance of such networks in Hanafi fiqh transmission.

Core Idea
Biographical listings certify the chain of knowledge transmission — the isnad of fiqh itself.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri provides a detailed list of scholars connected to the author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. While it may seem like a simple roster, such biographical networks are crucial for understanding how Hanafi fiqh was transmitted across generations and regions. The entries include teachers, students, and transmitters, each forming a link in the chain that validates the text you are studying.

Guided Path
1
Identify Entry Structure
Each entry typically includes the scholar's name, honorifics, birthplace, death year, and sometimes their relation to al-Maydani (e.g., student, transmitter). Look for these components.
Not all entries explicitly state the relation; footnotes may clarify.
2
Map Geographical Spread
Note the cities mentioned: Damascus, Medina, Baghdad, India. This shows the wide reach of al-Maydani's influence in the Hanafi world.
The Hanafi school was strong in these regions.
3
Evaluate Source Citations
The footnotes cite works like Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' and Tarikh Dimashq. Understand that these references establish the credibility of the information.
This is a scholarly practice ensuring traceability.
4
Recognize Manuscript Culture
The passage highlights al-Maydani's extensive copying of manuscripts (5000+ notebooks). This practice preserved and transmitted texts before printing.
Manuscript copying was a form of 'ilm in itself.
5
Connect to Hanafi Tradition
Reflect on how each named scholar contributes to the continuity of the Hanafi school. The isnad (chain) from al-Maydani back to earlier authorities is implicit.
This network strengthens the authority of al-Lubab.

(4) As in Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq, 1/250, and his death year is given as 1327 AH, while al-Bitar translated him in Hilyat al-Bashar, 2/684, and gave his death as 1331 AH.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of scholars connected to Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. The text continues from the previous page, detailing the scholars from number 6 to 13. Each entry includes the scholar's name, place of birth, death date, and sometimes additional remarks such as their works or their relation to al-Maydani. The footnotes provide sources for these biographies. This section serves to establish the scholarly lineage and network of al-Maydani, which is important for understanding the transmission of the Hanafi tradition. The scholars mentioned include figures from Damascus, Medina, Baghdad, and India, indicating the wide reach of al-Maydani's influence. For example, Sheikh Mustafa Kamal al-Sharif was a student of al-Maydani, as indicated in the footnote. Sheikh Habib al-Rahman al-Hindi was a transmitter from him. Sheikh Ali al-Watari was a muhaddith who also narrated from him. The later scholars like Nu'man al-Alusi, Salim al-Musuti, Muhammad Hashim al-Rifa'i, Salim Samara, and Mahmud Abu al-Shamat are all identified as either students or transmitters from al-Maydani. The passage highlights the importance of manuscript copying in the scholarly tradition, noting that al-Maydani copied thousands of notebooks. This biographical information is typical in the introductions of Islamic scholarly works to establish the credibility and chain of transmission of the author.

الفقيه الحنفي (al-faqīh al-ḥanafī): Jurist of the Hanafi school of law.

Biography of Shaykh Muhammad Hashim al-Rifa'i
Biography of a long-lived Hanafi scholar from Damascus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Shaykh Muhammad Hashim al-Rifa‘i and explain his significance as a long-lived Hanafi scholar.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar who lived 115 years and studied with al-Maidani.

This biography introduces us to a remarkable Hanafi scholar whose longevity spans two centuries. Understanding such figures helps us appreciate the chains of transmission and the enduring nature of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Note the full name: Muhammad Hashim ibn Muhammad Sa'id Abu Tawq al-Rifa'i. Recognize the honorific 'al-mu‘ammar' (the long-lived).

2
Extract dates and place
He was born in Damascus in 1267 AH and died there in 1382 AH. Calculate his age: 115 years.
The lifespan is exceptionally long, hence the title 'al-mu‘ammar'.
3
Identify teacher and connection
The footnote tells us he was a student of Shaykh al-Maidani, the author of the commentary Lubab al-Quduri.
Al-Maidani is a key Hanafi figure; this student-teacher link reinforces the chain of Hanafi transmission.
4
Understand the source context
This biography appears in a margin of a Hanafi fiqh text, referencing Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq. It shows how such biographical notes preserve scholarly lineage.
Biographical details like these are crucial for verifying chains of narration (sanad) in Islamic scholarship.

Interpreting a Hanafi Scholar's Biography
Biography of a Hanafi scholar with death year discrepancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract a scholar's teacher-student relationship from a biographical entry and evaluate the reliability of different death year reports.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography discloses the chain of learning, which is vital for verifying hadith and fiqh transmissions.

This lesson examines a short biographical note on Shaykh Salim Samara, a student of the famous Hanafi scholar al-Maidani. Beyond mere facts, we learn how biographical details establish the chain of knowledge (isnad) and how source criticism applies even to dates of death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and key dates
Read the name, birth year, death year, and location. Note the discrepancy in death year between the body (1331 AH) and the footnote (1327 AH from another source).
The footnote is commentary, not part of the original text.
2
Extract the teacher-student relationship
Identify the phrase 'qara’a ‘ala' (read to) and the teacher's name (al-Maidani). This indicates formal study and permission to transmit.
In Hanafi tradition, 'qara’a ‘alā' often implies ijazah (license) to teach.
3
Assess the authority of the biographical sources
The footnote cites two sources: Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq (gives 1327) and Hilyat al-Bashar (gives 1331). Which is more reliable? Consider the author's methodology and proximity to the subject.
Al-Bitar (author of Hilyat al-Bashar) was a contemporary, so his date is often preferred.
4
Apply the lesson to fiqh transmission
Knowing that Salim studied under al-Maidani means any fiqh rulings transmitted from him via Salim carry the weight of al-Maidani's authority. Discrepancies in death year affect the dating of his works and transmissions.
This is why biographical entries are part of usul al-hadith and fiqh.

[4] كما في تاريخ علماء دمشق ١ / ٢٥٠ ، وذكر وفاته سنة ١٣٢٧هـ، في حين أن البيطار ترجم له في حلية البشر ،٦٨٤/٢ ، وأرخ لوفاته سنة ١٣٣١هـ.

Biography of Mahmud Abu al-Shamat: A Hanafi Scholar and Sufi Shaykh
Biography of a Hanafi scholar with a cautionary annotation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Mahmud Abu al-Shamat, including his teachers, and explain the editor's caution regarding the Yashruti order.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's Sufi affiliation does not negate his fiqh, but requires discerning study.

The following passage introduces Shaykh Mahmud Abu al-Shamat, a Hanafi scholar who studied under the renowned al-Maidani and later became a prominent figure in the Yashruti Sufi order. The editor interjects a stern warning about the Yashruti order, alerting readers to questionable beliefs and practices. This lesson helps you parse this biographical entry and understand the importance of distinguishing a scholar's fiqh contributions from his spiritual affiliations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person
Locate the full name of the scholar, his birth and death years, and his birthplace. This establishes the basic historical context.
Note that the death year is in the margin.
2
Identify the Primary Teacher in Fiqh
The text states he 'took from Shaykh al-Maidani the Hanafi fiqh'. Al-Maidani is the author of the commentary (Sharh al-Quduri) you are studying. This connects this biography to your curriculum.
3
Identify the Spiritual Teacher and Order
He also 'studied under' Shaykh Ali al-Yashruti and took the Sufi path (tariqa) from him. He became the shaykh of the Yashruti order in Damascus.
The Yashruti order is a Sufi order originating from the Maghreb.
4
Understand the Editorial Caution
The editor inserts a footnote warning that the Yashruti order is associated with 'blameworthy and very objectionable' matters. This is a critical note for a student of Hanafi fiqh.
The editor cites sources for the biographies of al-Yashruti and his daughter Fatima.
5
Reflect on the Significance
Recognize that a scholar's association with a controversial group does not automatically discredit his fiqh, but it does require caution. The editor's warning alerts the reader to critically evaluate any teachings from that order.
This biography illustrates the complex intersections of madhhab and tasawwuf in Islamic history.

The Hanafi Mufti: Scholarly Lineage and Authority
Biographical entry for a Hanafi mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of a Hanafi mufti and explain why the teacher-student chain (silsila) is essential for authoritative fatwa-giving.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti's authority rests on authentic transmission from master to student.

This lesson focuses on Shaykh Salim al-Amidi, a Hanafi mufti who studied under the renowned scholar al-Maidani. His biography illustrates the critical importance of scholarly lineage (silsila) in the Hanafi madhhab. We will examine the formal title 'mufti' and the process of knowledge transmission that validates one's authority to issue fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his titles
Find the full name and titles of the scholar in the Arabic text. Note 'al-mufti' and 'al-hanafi' as key identifiers of his role and affiliation.
Titles like 'al-Imam' or 'al-Allamah' indicate high scholarly rank.
2
Understand the role of a mufti in the Hanafi school
A mufti is a qualified jurist who derives and issues fatwas. Unlike a qadi, he does not judge cases but provides legal opinions. His training under a recognized master ensures his rulings adhere to madhhab methodology.
In the Hanafi tradition, the mufti must know the source texts, the divergent rulings within the school, and the principles of tarjih.
3
Recognize the importance of the teacher-student relationship
The phrase 'qara’a ‘ala al-Maidani wa akhadha ‘anhu' indicates formal study and authorization. This chain (silsila) guarantees that the mufti's knowledge is authentically traced back to the early authorities.
This is akin to an ijazah (license) to transmit and teach.
4
Place the scholar in historical context
His birth (1268 AH) and death (1347 AH) place him in the late Ottoman period. A footnote cites Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq, showing the importance of biographical sources for verifying scholarly credentials.
Biographical dictionaries like this are key tools for establishing a scholar's reliability.

Source Text

الهامش:
[4] تاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر ٤٣١/١ .
The distinguished scholar, Shaykh Salim ibn Isma'il al-Amidi al-Bukhari al-Dimashqi, the Hanafi jurist and mufti, born in the year 1268 AH, and died in the year 1347 AH, and he read to al-Maidani and took from him [4] Margin: [4] Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq in the fourteenth century 1/431.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary

Key Terms
المفتي (al-muftī): The official jurist who issues fatwas; a high scholarly rank.

The Chain of Transmission: Why Scholarly Biographies Matter in Hanafi Fiqh
Author's biography and student list.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of scholarly lineages (silsila) in establishing the authority of a Hanafi text and state the names of at least three students of Shaykh al-Maydani.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's authority rests on his teachers and students—the silsila validates the transmission.

When you open a classical Hanafi fiqh commentary, you often encounter a biographical introduction listing the author's teachers and students. This is not dry history; it is a legal chain of transmission (silsila) that authenticates the knowledge. Shaykh al-Maydani's list of 18 students, including Ibn Abidin, demonstrates his scholarly standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the biographical elements
The passage gives the author's birth and death years, his teacher, and a list of 18 students arranged alphabetically.
Focus on the names and relationships.
2
Understand the function of the student list
In Hanafi tradition, such lists establish the author's credibility and the continuous chain of transmission (silsila) from the author back to the Prophet through reliable scholars.
This is similar to the isnad system in hadith.
3
Recognize key names
Note the inclusion of Muhammad Ala al-Din ibn Abidin, a major Hanafi authority and grandson of the famous Ibn Abidin (author of Radd al-Muhtar). This strengthens al-Maydani's prestige.
Other notable names include Sheikh Salim al-Bukhari and Sheikh Tahir al-Jazairi.
4
Connect to the purpose of the book
The commentary (Sharh al-Lubab) gains authority because it is written by a scholar with a verified chain of knowledge. The biography assures the reader that the content is soundly transmitted.
This practice is common in all Hanafi works.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the beginning of the book. It opens with a brief biography of the author, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (died 1355 AH), noting his birth year and his own teacher. It then lists several of his prominent students, including Muhammad Ala al-Din ibn Abidin (a well-known Hanafi jurist) and others. The list is arranged alphabetically. The passage includes footnotes referencing sources for the biographical information. This type of front matter is common in classical works to establish the scholarly chain and authority of the author.

The Scholarly Credibility of 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical introduction with list of teachers and praise of works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the scholarly authority of a Hanafi commentator by analyzing his teachers, the esteem of his peers, and the quality of his works as described in his biography.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is built on quality recognized by peers, not quantity of works.

Biographies of classical Hanafi scholars provide essential context for assessing the reliability of their works. This lesson examines the biography of 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, author of the widely used commentary Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab. By analyzing his teachers and the praise of his contemporaries, we learn to gauge the authority of his fiqh contributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his significance
Determine who 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani is and why his biography matters for Hanafi fiqh. He is the author of al-Lubab, a standard commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
Al-Lubab is a foundational text for Hanafi fiqh study.
2
List his teachers and note their prominence
From the list of names, identify teachers who are well-known Hanafi authorities, such as Muhammad Amin Abidin (the author of Radd al-Muhtar). This establishes al-Maydani's strong scholarly chain.
A scholar's teachers directly impact the authority of his riwayat and knowledge.
3
Analyze the description of his works
Read the praise from his contemporaries: they highlight quality over quantity, calling his works 'filled with benefits' and 'elegant treatises upon which the lights of acceptance shine.' This indicates high regard.
Such praise, especially when the scholar is still alive, adds credibility.
4
Evaluate the credibility of the biographical sources
The sources cited (e.g., Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, Hulyat al-Bashar) are reliable Hanafi biographers. This triangulation strengthens the biography's authenticity.
Always check the chain of transmission for biographical claims.

Seventh Section
His Works and Scholarly Output
Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, may Allah have mercy on him, was not among those who authored many works, but he was among those who excelled and were skilled in knowledge. His contemporary and the son of his own teacher, Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq bin Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, described his works, saying: 'His writings, which the beholder has the right to vie over and boast about, are filled with benefits that captivate minds and capture thoughts.'
His contemporary, companion, and one of his peers, the Allamah Sheikh Ahmad bin Muhammad al-Hadrawi al-Shafi'i al-Makki al-Hashimi, also said: 'He has a number of works and elegant treatises upon which the lights of acceptance shine.'
I say: This statement was said by al-Hadrawi while al-Maydani was still alive.
(1) From the words of the Allamah Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, in the introduction to his edition of al-Maydani's book 'Kashf al-Iltibas', p. 54.
(2) Hulyat al-Bashar 2/768
(3) Nuzhat al-Fikr 2/176.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The text first lists a number of scholars, likely his teachers or associates, including figures such as Habib al-Rahman al-Hindi and Muhammad Amin Abidin (the well-known Hanafi jurist). Then it discusses his scholarly output, noting that while he was not prolific, his works were of high quality. His contemporary Abd al-Razzaq al-Bitar praised his writings as rich in benefits, and another contemporary, Ahmad al-Hadrawi, mentioned his 'elegant treatises' that were well-received. The editor adds that these praises were made during al-Maydani's lifetime. The references at the end cite sources for these quotations. The biography establishes the author's credibility and the esteem in which he was held by his peers.

Key Terms
الميداني (al-Maydani): Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of the commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a prominent Hanafi scholar.
مؤلفاته (mu'allafatuhu): His writings or authored works. The text mentions that he was not prolific but his works were of high quality.

The Author and His Works: Al-Maidani's Scholarly Legacy
Biographical description of al-Maidani's scholarly production and praise from contemporaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two major works of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and explain their significance in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Maidani's al-Lubab and Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya embody quality over quantity in Hanafi scholarship.

This passage introduces us to the author of the very text we are studying—al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab. Understanding his scholarly approach and the reception of his works helps us appreciate the authority and reliability of this commentary. Al-Maidani was not a prolific author, but his works were meticulously crafted and highly praised by contemporaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his scholarly reputation
Read the opening lines: Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was not a prolific writer but excelled in quality and skill. Note the assessment by later scholars like Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah.
This sets the tone—quality over quantity.
2
Examine the praise from contemporaries
Two contemporaries commend his works: Abd al-Razzaq al-Baytar says they are 'filled with benefits' and Ahmad al-Hadrawi (a Shafi'i scholar) notes their 'lights of acceptance.'
Cross-madhhab recognition adds weight to his authority.
3
List the two major works
The passage lists al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab (commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar) and Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya (commentary on al-Tahawi's creed).
Al-Lubab is the focus of our course; the creed commentary shows his range.
4
Understand the significance of each work
Al-Lubab is a standard Hanafi fiqh commentary, widely used and printed multiple times during his lifetime. Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya is praised for its clarity, evidence, and completeness.
Both are foundational texts in their respective fields.
5
Reflect on the quantity vs. quality theme
Al-Maidani wrote fewer works but they achieved lasting acceptance. This challenges the notion that scholarly impact requires voluminous output.
Reflect on how this applies to your own learning.

Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, may Allah have mercy on him, was not among those who wrote excessively, but he was among those who excelled in writing and were skilled in knowledge. His contemporary and the son of his sheikh, Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq ibn Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, described his works, saying: 'His works, which the beholder has the right to compete over and boast about, are filled with benefits that fix thoughts and tie down ideas.' End quote.

(1) From the words of the Allamah Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, in the introduction to his verification of al-Maidani's book 'Kashf al-Iltibas', p. 54.

Chapter One: Biography of the Allamah Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
And his most famous book, 'al-Lubab', was published in multiple editions during his lifetime due to its many students, and Allah granted it acceptance more and more after his death, and after people came to know it and examine it.
I will list his works in order of their fame:
1- Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab.
It is a commentary on the Mukhtasar of Imam al-Quduri, who died in 428 AH, in Hanafi jurisprudence. The book was printed during the author's lifetime in more than one edition in a large volume, then its printing was repeated, and it was circulated widely among scholars and students. In the commonly available edition, it is in four parts, each part approximately 230 pages. The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is placed at the top of the pages in this edition. Detailed discussion of it will come later, if Allah wills, in a special chapter.
2- Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya.
It is a commentary on the creed composed by Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, who died in 321 AH, which he named 'Bayyan I'tiqad Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah'. It is a commentary, elegant in form and meaning, comprehensive and sufficient, supported by evidence from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. He clarified its ambiguities, unlocked its complexities, not too long to bore, nor too short to deprive, full of benefits, great in advantages, free from complicated and problematic issues.
The great scholars of his time praised it, commending both the author and the work with fragrant praise, affirming that it is a reliable commentary with no criticism against it, and that it contains the essence.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This is a biographical passage concerning the Hanafi jurist Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, author of 'al-Lubab' (the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar). The passage begins by describing his approach to authorship: he was not prolific but was meticulous and innovative in his scholarship. Two contemporaries praise his works: Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq al-Baytar states that his writings are filled with benefits that captivate the intellect, and Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi (a Shafi'i scholar) notes that his works have 'lights of acceptance,' meaning they were well-received. The passage then lists his most famous works. The first is 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab', a commentary on Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, which is the very book we are studying. It was published multiple times during his lifetime and remains widely circulated. The second is 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya', a commentary on the creed of Imam al-Tahawi, praised for its clarity, evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, and its freedom from complicated issues. This passage provides important context for understanding the author's scholarly standing and the nature of his works.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The book title meaning 'The Core' or 'The Essence'; it is al-Maidani's commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar in Hanafi fiqh.
العقيدة الطحاوية (al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya): A creedal work by Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi outlining the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

Biography of Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and His Commentary Method
Biographical account of author and his commentary style

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of al-sharh al-mazji and explain why al-Tahawiyyah is considered a foundational Hanafi creedal text.

Core Idea
Al-sharh al-mazji interweaves text and commentary to teach Hidayah efficiently—a distinct Hanafi pedagogical tool.

This lesson introduces the scholar Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and his commentary style. Understanding his method helps us appreciate how Hanafi texts have been traditionally taught. The passage also underscores the importance of al-Tahawiyyah as the creed of Abu Hanifa, central to Hanafi identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his work
Locate the name of the author and the title of his commentary. Note that his full name is Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maidani and his work is al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri.
Al-Maidani completed this commentary at age 34, showing his early scholarly achievement.
2
Understand the sharh al-mazji method
Examine the description of 'al-sharh al-mazji' – a mixed commentary where the commentator's explanation is interwoven with the original text. This method helps students follow the text and explanation concurrently.
This is a common pedagogical technique in Hanafi madrasas.
3
Recognize the importance of al-Tahawiyyah
Read the author's introduction praising al-Tahawiyyah. Note that he calls it the creed of Abu Hanifa and highlights its comprehensive coverage of Islamic creed despite its small size.
Al-Tahawiyyah is a foundational text for Hanafi theology (Maturidism).
4
Connect to Abu Hanifa's authority
The author explicitly states that al-Tahawiyyah represents the creed of Imam Abu Hanifa. This establishes the work's authority within the Hanafi school.
This reinforces the continuity of Hanafi doctrine from the founder to later scholars.

First Chapter: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. It is a commentary according to what is called the mixed commentary (al-sharh al-mazji) between the wording of the text and the commentary. Al-Maidani completed its authorship in the year 1256 AH, at the age of thirty-four. This commentary was published in edited form in (160) pages, edited by Dr. Muhammad Muti' al-Hafiz and Ustadh Muhammad Riyad al-Malih, issued by Dar al-Fikr in Damascus, and the date of the completion of their editing for the first edition was 1390 AH, then the second edition was issued in 1402 AH, and the endorsements of scholars were placed at the end of the book. And it appears in the author's introduction: ... Thereafter: says the one hoping for attainment of aspirations, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maidani, may Allah forgive his sins and conceal his faults in both abodes: Since the science of tawhid is the foundation of building support, and the noblest of sciences due to the object of knowledge, but with the condition of not departing from the meaning derived from the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the upright. And the creed famously known as 'The Creed of al-Tahawi' is among the best of what has been authored in this regard, and this does not require proof, because despite its small size and ease of understanding, it has not left any principle from the principles of religious creed except that it made you aware of it, and it has not left any of its fundamental and important issues except that it explicitly or implicitly mentioned them. And it is sufficient that it is the creed of the Imam of Imams, and the lamp of this nation, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, may mercy and good pleasure be upon him... end.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. It begins by stating that his work 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' is a mixed commentary (sharh mazji), meaning it interweaves the original matn text with the explanation, a common pedagogical style in the Hanafi tradition. He completed this commentary in 1256 AH at the young age of 34, indicating his scholarly prodigiousness. The commentary was later published in 160 pages with editing by two contemporary scholars. The passage then includes a lengthy excerpt from al-Maidani's introduction to a separate work on creed, likely his commentary on al-Tahawiyyah. In this introduction, al-Maidani praises the science of tawhid as the foundation of faith and extols the famous creed of al-Tahawi, noting that despite its brevity, it covers all essential principles of Islamic creed. He emphasizes that it represents the creed of Imam Abu Hanifa, indicating the Hanafi orthodox position. This biographical section serves to establish the author's credentials and the scholarly value of his works.

Key Terms
الشرح المزجي (al-sharh al-mazji): A style of commentary where the commentator's explanation is interwoven with the original text, often distinguished by markers or brackets.
عقيدة الطحاوي (al-ʿAqīdah al-Ṭaḥāwiyyah): A classical Sunni creedal work by Imam al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), summarizing the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah according to the Hanafi school.

Al-Maidani's sharh mazji method and his endorsement of al-Tahawiyyah exemplify the Hanafi tradition's emphasis on pedagogical clarity and creedal continuity from Abu Hanifa.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
- كشف الالتباس عما أورده الإمام البخاري على بعض الناس . وهي رسالة لطيفة جاء نصها مطبوعاً في (٤٠) صفحة، بتحقيق العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله، وفي (١٠٦) صفحة بنصها ومقدمات محققها، وتاريخ الطبعة الأولى منها سنة ١٤١٤هـ، معتمداً على نسخة واحدة كانت عند حفيد المؤلف، كما سيأتي ذكر ذلك بعد قليل.
وقد يسر الله لي صورةً عن نسخة أخرى مخطوطة منها، نُسخت سنة ١٢٩٨هـ، بخط محمد ابن الشيخ عبد القادر، وفيها أن المؤلف انتهى منها في غرة محرم سنة ۱۲۹۱هـ ، وهذه النسخة عليها رقـم : (۳۹۳۷) عام)، وكأنه رقمها في مخطوطات الظاهرية بدمشق، والله أعلم، وتقع في (۱۲) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (٢٥) سطراً. والمراد بقول الإمام البخاري : بعض الناس»: الإمام أبو حنيفة رحمهما الله تعالى.

وقد اعترضه كثير من الأئمة بممانعات قوية، وأجابوا عن اعتراضاته بأجوبة سديدة مَرْضيَّة، فأحببتُ أن أذكر ما قالوه، بعد ذكر ما قال، ليرتفع الشك، ويتبيَّن الحال، لما اشتهر عند الكثير، والجم الغفير، أن المراد بقول البخاري: قال بعض الناس هو المجتهد المقدم الإمام الأعظم.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
- 'Kashf al-Iltebas 'amma Awradahu al-Imam al-Bukhari 'ala Ba'd al-Nas' (Removing Confusion Regarding What Imam al-Bukhari Raised Against Some People). This is a refined treatise, its text printed in (40) pages, edited by the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, and in (106) pages with its text and the introductions of its editors, with the first edition dating to 1414 AH, based on a single manuscript that was with the author's grandson, as will be mentioned shortly.
Allah facilitated for me a copy of another manuscript of it, copied in the year 1298 AH, in the handwriting of Muhammad, son of Sheikh Abdul Qadir, in which the author states he completed it at the beginning of Muharram 1291 AH. This manuscript bears the number (3937 general), and it seems it was catalogued in the Zahiriyya manuscripts in Damascus, and Allah knows best. It consists of (12) folios, with (25) lines per page. What is meant by Imam al-Bukhari's statement 'some people' is: Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on them both.
The author's introduction states:
'... This is a treatise in which I mention what Imam al-Bukhari mentioned in his 'Sahih' of subsidiary issues, expressing them by his saying: 'Some people said,' and he objected to them with the utmost objection, to the point that he attributed to the speaker leniency and weakness, and in some of them: 'He contradicted the Book, the Sunnah, and most of the imams.'
Many imams objected to him with strong refutations, and they responded to his objections with correct and acceptable answers. So I wanted to mention what they said, after mentioning what he said, so that doubt may be removed and the situation becomes clear, because it has become well-known among many and the general multitude that what is meant by Bukhari's statement 'Some people said' is the leading mujtahid, the Greatest Imam.
Hearing such things about this Imam may perhaps cause some blind followers to fall into doubt and confusion, although attributing some of them to him is incorrect, because his statement is clearly contrary to them, and the rest, even if it is from his school, he was not alone in it, but rather other mujtahids and earlier imams agreed with him on it...' End quote.
In this treatise, al-Maydani discussed twenty-five issues, and explained what is meant by them in a brief, refined manner. Its editor, the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, elaborated in its editing, and added in removing confusion, thus offering a gift to every rememberer and forgetter.
4- 'Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak' (The Gift of the Pious Regarding the Virtue of the Siwak).
The author's introduction states: '... As for what follows: This is a treatise containing excellent benefits and eight pearls, which I have plucked from the books of the earlier scholars, from the jurists and hadith scholars, and I have named it: 'Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak.' I arranged it into an introduction, three chapters, and a conclusion: the introduction is about the definition of siwak and its rulings; the first chapter is about its time; the second chapter is about its method of use; the third chapter is about its benefits; and the conclusion is about the best types of siwak.' End quote.
The treatise has been printed under the editing of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, along with other benefits that the editor included with it, increasing its beauty and elegance in form and meaning. The treatise came out as edited in
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of the book 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri', the eminent Hanafi scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH). The compiler of the current work provides details about two of al-Maydani's treatises. The first is 'Kashf al-Iltebas 'amma Awradahu al-Imam al-Bukhari 'ala Ba'd al-Nas', a defense of Imam Abu Hanifa against criticisms made by Imam al-Bukhari in his Sahih under the phrase 'qala ba'd al-nas' (some people said). Al-Maydani collected responses from earlier scholars to clear the confusion, showing that Bukhari's criticism either did not apply to Abu Hanifa or was not unique to him. The second treatise is 'Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak', a concise work on the virtues and rulings of using the siwak (tooth-stick), organized into an introduction, three chapters, and a conclusion. Both works were edited by the late scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah. The passage serves as front matter setting the context for al-Maydani's scholarly contributions.

Key Terms
بعض الناس (ba'd al-nas): literally 'some people'; a phrase used by Imam al-Bukhari in his Sahih to refer to individuals he criticizes, often understood as referring to Imam Abu Hanifa.
السواك (al-siwak): The tooth-stick used for cleaning teeth, recommended in Islam.
التحقيق (al-tahqiq): Scholarly editing; the process of verifying and annotating a manuscript for publication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Scholarly Contributions of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical introduction to the author and description of his writings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main works of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and explain their significance in Hanafi fiqh and hadith studies.

Core Idea
Sheikh al-Maidani authored works on fiqh, hadith chains, and the siwak, reflecting the interconnectedness of Islamic sciences.

This lesson introduces you to the scholarly profile of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, a Hanafi jurist and hadith scholar. Through a brief passage from his biography, you will learn about three of his key works: a concise treatise on twenty-five fiqh issues, a focused monograph on the siwak (toothstick), and a thabat (collection of hadith chains) for his teacher. Understanding the breadth of his writings helps you appreciate how Hanafi scholars combined fiqh, hadith, and biography to preserve and transmit knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name
Locate the name 'Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani' in the passage. Note that he is also referred to as 'al-Ghanimi al-Maidani' in the colophon of the thabat.
His full name is Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani, a Hanafi scholar from Damascus.
2
Recognize the three works mentioned
The passage describes three distinct works: a treatise on twenty-five issues, a book titled 'Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak', and a thabat compiled for Sheikh Abdul Rahman al-Kuzbari.
Each work serves a different purpose: fiqh rulings, a specific sunnah practice, and hadith chain documentation.
3
Understand the nature of each work
The first is a brief fiqh treatise, the second is a detailed study of siwak divided into an introduction, three chapters, and a conclusion, and the third is a thabat – a list of hadith chains with ijazas.
A thabat is not a fiqh work but a tool for preserving transmission links.
4
Appreciate the verification work of later scholars
Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah verified and added to the first two works, and later editors like Umar al-Nashuqati verified the thabat. This shows the ongoing tradition of scholarly editing and preservation.
Verification (tahqiq) is a critical part of Islamic scholarship, ensuring texts are accurately transmitted.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

الغفير، أن المراد بقول البخاري: قال بعض الناس هو المجتهد المقدم الإمام الأعظم.
وسماع مثل ذلك عن هذا الإمام، ربما يُوقع بعض المقلّدين في الشك والإيهام، مع أن نسبة بعضها إليه غير صحيح، لأن قوله بخلافهـا صريح، والباقي وإن كان من مذهبه لكنه لم ينفرد بـه، بـل وافقـه عليـه غيره من المجتهدين، والأئمة السابقين...». اهـ

٤- تحفة النُّسَاكَ في فَضل السَّوَاك .
:
جاء في مقدمة المؤلف: «.. أما بعد فهذه رسالة مشتملة على فوائد حسان، ودُرَر ثمان، اقتطفتُها من كتب الأقدمين، من الفقهاء والمحدثين، وسمَّيْتُها : تحفة النساك في فضل السواك»، ورتبتها على مقدمة، وثلاثة أبواب، وخاتمة المقدمة: في تعريف السواك، وأحكامه، والباب الأول : في وقته والباب الثاني: في كيفية استعماله، والباب الثالث في منافعه والخاتمة : في أفضل أنواع السواك». اهـ
وقد تم طبع الرسالة بتحقيق العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله تعالى، مع فوائد أخرى ضمها إليها محققها، زادت في حليتها وجمالها صورةً ومعنى ، وقد جاءت الرسالة محققة في (١٠٤) صفحة من القطع الصغير، وصدرت الطبعة الأولى سنة ١٤١٤هـ.

ه ثبت الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن محمد الكزبري الصغير، العلامة المحدث الكبير، المولود سنة ١١٨٤هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
جَمَع هذا الثَّبَت، وخرجه له تلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، إلا أن هذا لم يشتهر ، ولم يُذكر ذلك في الطبعات السابقة للثّبت. وقد طبع هذا الثبت محققاً في (٩٠) صفحة، ، ضمن كتاب عنوانه : (مجموع الأثبات الحديثية لآل الكزبري الدمشقيين وسيرهم وإجازاتهم)، من صفحة (۲۷۷) إلى صفحة (٣٦٦).
حقق هذا المجموع: الأستاذ عمر بن موفق النشوقاتي، وطبع في دار البشائر الإسلامية، بيروت، عام ١٤٢٨هـ.
وكان قد طبعه سابقاً شيخنا العلامة المحدث المفنن الشيخ محمد ياسين الفاداني المكي، المتوفى سنة ١٤١٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى، وجزاه عنا خير الجزاء، ولم يُذكر في طبعته أنه من تخريج الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وتم نشر هذه الطبعة في دار البصائر بدمشق، عام ١٤٠٣هـ.

فقد
وأما الطبعة الجديدة بتحقيق الأستاذ عمر بن موفق النشوقاتي، وضع فيها محققها جزاه الله خيراً صورة لآخـر صـفحـة مـن مخطوط الثبت، وفيها: «أنه من جَمْع الفقير كثير التواني عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، في ٩ شوال سنة ١٢٦٠هـ». اهـ، أي كان له
Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani

... that what al-Bukhari meant by 'some people said' is the leading mujtahid, the greatest Imam.
Hearing such things about this Imam might cause some followers to fall into doubt and confusion, even though attributing some of them to him is incorrect, because his statement contrary to them is explicit, and the rest, even if it is from his school, he was not alone in it, but rather other mujtahids and earlier imams agreed with him on it.' (end quote)

Al-Maidani spoke in this treatise on twenty-five issues, and explained their meanings in a brief and elegant manner, and its editor, the scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, elaborated in its verification and increased in removing confusion, thereby gifting every mindful and forgetful person.

4- Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak (The Gift of the Devout on the Virtue of the Siwak)

From the author's introduction: '... To proceed: This is a treatise containing beautiful benefits and eight pearls, which I have gathered from the books of the ancients, from the jurists and hadith scholars, and I named it: Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak. I arranged it into an introduction, three chapters, and a conclusion. The introduction: on the definition of siwak and its rulings. The first chapter: on its time. The second chapter: on its manner of use. The third chapter: on its benefits. The conclusion: on the best types of siwak.' (end quote)

The treatise has been printed with the verification of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, along with other benefits that its editor included, adding to its beauty and grace in form and meaning. The treatise was verified in (104) pages of small size, and the first edition was published in 1414 AH.

5- Thabat of Sheikh Abdul Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kuzbari al-Saghir, the great hadith scholar, born in 1184 AH and died in 1262 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.

His student Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani collected this thabat and prepared it for him, but it did not become famous and was not mentioned in previous editions of the thabat. This thabat was printed in a verified form in (90) pages within a book entitled: 'Majmu' al-Athbat al-Hadithiyya li Al al-Kuzbari al-Dimashqiyyin wa Sirihim wa Ijazatihim' (Collection of Hadith Chains of the Kuzbari Family of Damascus and Their Biographies and Certifications), from page (277) to page (366).

This collection was verified by Professor Umar ibn Muwaffaq al-Nashuqati and printed by Dar al-Basha'ir al-Islamiyya, Beirut, in 1428 AH.

Previously, our teacher, the great hadith scholar and polymath Sheikh Muhammad Yasin al-Fadani al-Makki, who died in 1410 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, had printed it, may Allah reward him well, but his edition did not mention that it was prepared by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. This edition was published by Dar al-Basa'ir in Damascus in 1403 AH.

As for the new edition verified by Professor Umar ibn Muwaffaq al-Nashuqati, may Allah reward him well, its editor included an image of the last page of the thabat manuscript, which states: 'It is the compilation of the poor, often negligent, Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani, on 9 Shawwal 1260 AH.' (end quote), meaning it was his.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, providing details about his life and works. The text begins by addressing a misconception about the great Imam Abu Hanifa, clarifying that some statements attributed to him are either false or shared by other scholars. Then it lists two of al-Maidani's works: The first is a treatise on twenty-five issues (likely a risala on points of fiqh), and the second is 'Tuhfat al-Nusak fi Fadl al-Siwak,' which is a work on the use of the miswak (toothstick) in Islamic practice. The author's son or editor, Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, provided thorough verification. The third work mentioned is a thabat (a list of chains of transmission) for Sheikh Abdul Rahman al-Kuzbari, which al-Maidani compiled. The passage details the publication history of these works, showing the scholarly tradition of verification and chain transmission.

Key Terms
ثبت (thabat): A list of hadith chains or a collection of isnads (chains of transmission) compiled by a scholar, often containing ijazas (certifications) and biographical information.
السواك (al-siwak): A piece of twig used for cleaning the teeth, typically from the arak tree; its use is recommended in Islamic hygiene practices.

Al-Maidani's Compilation of the Thabat of al-Kuzbari
Biographical account of al-Maidani's compilation of a thabat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of a thabat in the Hanafi tradition and identify the role of al-Maidani in compiling the Thabat of al-Kuzbari.

Core Idea
A thabat preserves a scholar's chain of transmission; al-Maidani compiled one for his teacher, a fact only later discovered.

In the Hanafi tradition, a thabat is a vital document that records a scholar's teachers, licenses, and chains of transmission. This lesson explores a specific thabat compiled by the renowned Hanafi commentator al-Maidani for his teacher al-Kuzbari, revealing how manuscript research can uncover hidden scholarly contributions.

Guided Path
1
Define 'thabat'
Identify the Arabic term 'thabat' and its meaning: a list of chains of transmission (isnad) and licenses (ijazat) that a scholar possesses.
Thabats are crucial for verifying the authenticity of narrations.
2
Identify the compiler and beneficiary
From the passage, note that al-Maidani compiled the thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari, who is the subject of the thabat.
This relationship shows the student-teacher bond in preserving knowledge.
3
Understand the late attribution
Recognize that earlier editions did not name al-Maidani as compiler; only later critical editions revealed this through manuscript evidence.
This highlights the importance of manuscript study.
4
Analyze the supporting evidence
The passage cites additional sources: a biography by Abu al-Khayr 'Abidin and al-Kuzbari's own ijaza, both confirming al-Maidani's role.
Multiple confirmations strengthen the attribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني (١٠٤) صفحة من القطع الصغير، وصدرت الطبعة الأولى سنة ١٤١٤هـ. ثبت الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن محمد الكزبري الصغير، العلامة المحدث الكبير، المولود سنة ١١٨٤هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. جَمَع هذا الثَّبَت، وخرجه له تلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، إلا أن هذا لم يشتهر ، ولم يُذكر ذلك في الطبعات السابقة للثّبت. وقد طبع هذا الثبت محققاً في (٩٠) صفحة، ضمن كتاب عنوانه : (مجموع الأثبات الحديثية لآل الكزبري الدمشقيين وسيرهم وإجازاتهم)، من صفحة (۲۷۷) إلى صفحة (٣٦٦). حقق هذا المجموع: الأستاذ عمر بن موفق النشوقاتي، وطبع في دار البشائر الإسلامية، بيروت، عام ١٤٢٨هـ. وكان قد طبعه سابقاً شيخنا العلامة المحدث المفنن الشيخ محمد ياسين الفاداني المكي، المتوفى سنة ١٤١٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى، وجزاه عنا خير الجزاء، ولم يُذكر في طبعته أنه من تخريج الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وتم نشر هذه الطبعة في دار البصائر بدمشق، عام ١٤٠٣هـ. وأما الطبعة الجديدة بتحقيق الأستاذ عمر بن موفق النشوقاتي، وضع فيها محققها جزاه الله خيراً صورة لآخـر صـفحـة مـن مخطوط الثبت، وفيها: «أنه من جَمْع الفقير كثير التواني عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، في ٩ شوال سنة ١٢٦٠هـ». اهـ، أي كان له من العمر ٣٨ سنة. (١٠٥) وقد سبق المحقق الأستاذ النشوقاتي إلى ذكر هذه الفائدة، وأن هذا الثبت من جَمْع الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، سبقه الشيخ أبو الخير عابدین محمد أحمد بن عبد الغني (١٢٦٩هـ ـ ١٣٤٣هـ)، وذلك في ترجمة كتبها للكزبري، نقلها بنصها أحمد تيمور باشا في «أعــلام الفكر الإسلامي»(۱)، وقد جاء فيها: «أخذ الكزبري عن جملة ممن أسانيدهم في غايــة العلـو والاشتهار، يقاربون الخمسين كما ذكره الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في الثّبت الذي جَمَعَه له». اهـ وأيضاً يقول الكزبري صاحب الثبت في إجازته لإبراهيم الحافظ (۲) : «أجزتُ المذكور بكل ما لي من رواية عن مشايخي الأعلام، مما تضمنه ثَبَتْ هذا الفقير الذي جَمَعَـه علـى لساني بعض أولاد القلب الكرام. اهـ يريد به الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني. وهكذا جمع الشيخ الميداني في هذا الثبت شيوخ شيخه الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن محمد الكزبري، وإجازاته، وأسانيده في الكتب الستة، وغيرها من كتب الحديث، ومختلف العلوم. (١) ص ٢٢٦ . (۲) ص ٤٨٠ من الطبعة المحققة في مجموع الأثبات الحديثية لآل الكزبري».
Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. A small octavo page (104), and the first edition was published in the year 1414 AH. The Thabat of Sheikh Abdul Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kuzbari al-Saghir, the great scholar and hadith master, born in 1184 AH and died in 1262 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. His student Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani compiled this Thabat and transcribed it for him, but this fact did not become well-known and was not mentioned in previous editions of the Thabat. This Thabat was printed in a critical edition of (90) pages, within a book titled: 'Collection of Hadith Thabats of the al-Kuzbari family of Damascus, their biographies and licenses', from pages (277) to (366). This collection was edited by Professor Umar ibn Muwaffaq al-Nashuqati, and printed by Dar al-Basha'ir al-Islamiyya, Beirut, in the year 1428 AH. Previously, our teacher, the erudite scholar and hadith specialist Sheikh Muhammad Yasin al-Fadani al-Makki (d. 1410 AH, may Allah have mercy on him and reward him well) had printed it, but he did not mention in his edition that it was compiled by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. That edition was published by Dar al-Basa'ir in Damascus in 1403 AH. As for the new edition edited by Professor Umar ibn Muwaffaq al-Nashuqati, the editor (may Allah reward him) included a photograph of the last page of the manuscript of the Thabat, which states: 'Compiled by the needy one, often negligent, Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani, on 9 Shawwal 1260 AH.' That is, he was 38 years old. (105) The editor, Professor al-Nashuqati, preceded others in mentioning this benefit, that this Thabat was compiled by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. He was preceded by Sheikh Abu al-Khayr 'Abidin Muhammad Ahmad ibn Abdul Ghani (1269-1343 AH) in a biography he wrote for al-Kuzbari, which Ahmad Taymur Pasha quoted verbatim in 'A'lam al-Fikr al-Islami' (1), in which it said: 'Al-Kuzbari studied under a group of scholars whose chains of transmission are exceedingly high and well-known, nearly fifty as stated by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani in the Thabat he compiled for him.' Also, al-Kuzbari, the author of the Thabat, says in his license (ijaza) to Ibrahim al-Hafiz (2): 'I have licensed the aforementioned with everything I have in narration from my esteemed teachers, as contained in this Thabat of this poor one, which was compiled on my behalf by some of the noble children of the heart.' Meaning Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Thus, Sheikh al-Maidani compiled in this Thabat the teachers of his teacher Sheikh Abdul Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kuzbari, his licenses, and his chains of transmission in the six major hadith collections and other hadith books and various sciences. (1) p. 226. (2) p. 480 of the critical edition in 'Collection of Hadith Thabats of the al-Kuzbari Family'.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the first chapter of al-Maidani's book al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. The author discusses the scholarly output of al-Maidani, specifically his compilation of a thabat (a list of chains of transmission and licenses) for his teacher al-Kuzbari. The passage clarifies that al-Maidani's role as compiler was not widely known in earlier editions; only later critical work revealed it. It also notes that al-Maidani was 38 years old when he completed the work in 1260 AH. The passage cites additional confirmation from a biography by Ahmad Taymur Pasha and from al-Kuzbari's own ijaza, which mentions that the thabat was compiled on his behalf by 'some of the noble children of the heart'—a reference to al-Maidani. This shows al-Maidani's dedication to preserving the scholarly chains of his teacher.

Key Terms
ثبت (thabat): A list of chains of transmission (isnad) and licenses (ijazat) of a scholar, documenting his teachers and the works he is authorized to transmit.
إجازة (ijaza): A license granted by a scholar to a student, authorizing the student to transmit the scholar's works and traditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Maidani, best known for his commentary on al-Quduri, also compiled his teacher's thabat, demonstrating his dedication to preserving scholarly chains.

The Scholarly Life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: Thabat, Ijazah, and His Works
Biographical introduction to the author and his scholarly works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of a thabat and ijazah in Hanafi scholarship and identify the subject of al-Maidani's treatise on menstrual rulings.

Core Idea
A thabat records a scholar's chains of transmission, preserving the living link to prophetic knowledge.

This passage introduces us to the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, the author of al-Lubab. It describes his role in compiling a thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari, and highlights one of his specialized treatises on the fiqh of menstruation. Understanding these biographical details helps us appreciate how Hanafi knowledge was transmitted and how scholars like al-Maidani contributed to specific fiqh topics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his role
Who is Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani? What is his main work mentioned in this passage?
He is the author of al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri.
2
Understand the thabat
What is a thabat? Who compiled it for whom according to the passage?
A thabat is a collection of chains and permissions. Al-Maidani compiled it for his teacher al-Kuzbari.
3
Recognize the ijazah
How did al-Kuzbari acknowledge al-Maidani's compilation in his ijazah?
Al-Kuzbari referred to the thabat compiled 'on his tongue' by al-Maidani.
4
Examine the treatise
What is the subject of al-Matalib al-Mustatabah? Why is it important in Hanafi fiqh?
It deals with menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and irregular bleeding; relevant for muftis.
5
Connect to broader scholarship
What other works of al-Maidani are mentioned? How do they relate to his expertise?
Works on morphology, creed, and hadith defense show his wide learning.

وقد سبق المحقق الأستاذ النشوقاتي إلى ذكر هذه الفائدة، وأن هذا الثبت من جَمْع الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، سبقه الشيخ أبو الخير عابدین محمد أحمد بن عبد الغني (١٢٦٩هـ ـ ١٣٤٣هـ)، وذلك بن في ترجمة كتبها للكزبري، نقلها بنصها أحمد تيمور باشا في «أعــلام الفكر الإسلامي»(۱)، وقد جاء فيها: «أخذ الكزبري عن جملة ممن أسانيدهم في غايــة العلـو والاشتهار، يقاربون الخمسين كما ذكره الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في الثّبت الذي جَمَعَه له». اهـ

(۲) ص ٤٨٠ من الطبعة المحققة في مجموع الأثبات الحديثية لآل الكزبري».

-٦ - المَطالِب المُستطابة في الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة.
وهي مخطوطة بعد لم تُطبع، وتقع في (٢٥) صفحة.
وقد ذكرها الميداني في كتابه: «اللباب»، وأحال عليها لمن أراد التوسع في موضوعها، فقد قال وهو يتكلم عن المحيرة في حيضها : وقد استوفينا الكلام عليها في رسالتنا في الدماء، المسماة بـ: المطالب المستطابة في الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة»، فمن رام استيفاء الكلام، وشفاء الأوام، فعليه بها، فإنها وافية بالمرام (۱). اهـ
ومن النسخ المخطوطة لهذه الرسالة ما ذكره العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله في مقدمة تحقيقه لرسالة الميداني : «كشف الالتباس»، حيث قال: «وقد وقفت في دمشق في (٢٠) من المحرم سنة (۱۳۷۸هـ)، على مجموع مخطوط، فيه عدة عدة من مؤلفات الميداني رحمه الله تعالى فمنها وهو أول المجموع: ۱- شرح المراح»، في الصرف، في (۱۳۳) صفحة من القطع الوسط.
٢- وثانيها: «شرح عقيدة الإمام الطحاوي»، في (١٠٠ صفحة). وثالثها : كشف الالتباس عما أورده الإمام البخاري على بعض الناس»، في (٣٥) صفحة.
ورابعها : «المطالب المستطابة في الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة»
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
And the investigator Professor al-Nashuqati preceded in mentioning this benefit, and that this thabat is from the compilation of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani; preceded by Sheikh Abu al-Khair 'Abidin Muhammad Ahmad bin Abdul Ghani (1269 AH - 1343 AH), and that [؟] in a biography he wrote for al-Kuzbari, which Ahmad Taymur Pasha quoted in full in 'A'lam al-Fikr al-Islami' (1), in which it came: 'Al-Kuzbari took from a number of those whose chains are of the utmost elevation and fame, approaching fifty, as Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani mentioned in the thabat he compiled for him.' End quote.
And also al-Kuzbari, author of the thabat, says in his ijazah to Ibrahim al-Hafiz (2): 'I have authorized the aforementioned with all that I have of narration from my eminent teachers, which is included in this thabat of this humble one, compiled on my tongue by some of the generous people of the heart.' End quote. By this he means Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Thus Sheikh al-Maidani gathered in this thabat the teachers of his teacher Sheikh Abdul Rahman bin Muhammad al-Kuzbari, and his ijazat, and his chains in the Six Books and other hadith books and various sciences.
(1) p. 226.
(2) p. 480 from the critical edition in 'Majmu' al-Athbat al-Hadithiyyah li-Al al-Kuzbari'.

-6- Al-Matalib al-Mustatabah fi al-Hayd wa al-Nifas wa al-Istihadah.
It is a manuscript not yet printed, comprising (25) pages.
Al-Maidani mentioned it in his book 'al-Lubab', and referred to it for those who wish to expand on the topic, as he said while discussing the confused woman regarding her menstruation: 'We have fully discussed it in our treatise on bloods, entitled Al-Matalib al-Mustatabah fi al-Hayd wa al-Nifas wa al-Istihadah.' So whoever desires complete discussion and healing of ailments should refer to it, for it is sufficient for the purpose. (1) End quote.
Among the manuscript copies of this treatise is what the scholar Sheikh Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah mentioned in his introduction to his edition of al-Maidani's treatise 'Kashf al-Iltibas', where he said: 'I stopped in Damascus on the 20th of Muharram 1378 AH at a manuscript collection containing several of al-Maidani's works. Among them, and it is the first of the collection: 1- Sharh al-Mirah in morphology, in 133 pages octavo.
2- Second: Sharh 'Aqidat al-Imam al-Tahawi in 100 pages.
3- Third: Kashf al-Iltibas 'amma awradahu al-Imam al-Bukhari 'ala ba'd al-nas, in 35 pages.
4- Fourth: Al-Matalib al-Mustatabah fi al-Hayd wa al-Nifas wa al-Istihadah.'
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of al-Lubab, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It begins by noting that the researcher al-Nashuqati had previously mentioned the benefit of the thabat compiled by al-Maidani for his teacher al-Kuzbari. The same thabat was also mentioned by Ahmad Taymur Pasha, who quoted al-Kuzbari's own words about the high chains of his teachers. Additionally, the text quotes al-Kuzbari's ijazah given to Ibrahim al-Hafiz, confirming that al-Maidani compiled the thabat on his behalf. The passage then moves to list one of al-Maidani's works: 'Al-Matalib al-Mustatabah fi al-Hayd wa al-Nifas wa al-Istihadah', a treatise on menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and irregular uterine bleeding (istihadah). Al-Maidani himself refers to this treatise in his main work al-Lubab, directing readers who wish for a fuller discussion on the topic to consult it. The passage concludes by citing the scholar Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah, who discovered a manuscript collection containing several of al-Maidani's works, including Sharh al-Mirah (on morphology), Sharh 'Aqidat al-Imam al-Tahawi, Kashf al-Iltibas (a defense of Imam al-Bukhari), and the aforementioned treatise on bloods. This provides valuable context about the author's scholarship and the interconnected nature of his writings.

Key Terms
الثبت (al-thabat): A record or collection of a scholar's chains of transmission (asanid) and scholarly permissions (ijazat), often compiled for a specific person.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): A formal permission from a teacher to a student to transmit or teach his works or narrations.
المطالب المستطابة في الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة (al-Matalib al-Mustatabah fi al-Hayd wa al-Nifas wa al-Istihadah): Title of al-Maidani's treatise: 'The Desirable Objectives on Menstruation, Postpartum Bleeding, and Irregular Bleeding'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's thabat compilation and his treatise on women's bloods exemplify the Hanafi tradition's emphasis on documented chains and specialized fiqh works.

Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and His Hanafi Treatises
Biographical introduction and listing of works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the subject matter of al-Maydani's two treatises and explain the Hanafi legal concept of 'Mashadd al-Maskah'.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's treatises address essential Hanafi rulings on worship and property rights.

This lesson introduces you to the life and works of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab. His concise treatises cover foundational Islamic beliefs and acts of worship, as well as specialized Hanafi legal issues like compensation for vacating leased property. Understanding his works helps you trace the development of Hanafi legal thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of al-Maydani's main treatise
The passage states he wrote a concise work on tawhid and rulings of worship (tahara, salah, zakat, sawm, hajj) based on the hadith of Jibril. Note that it is meant for beginners.
2
Analyze the treatise 'Mashadd al-Maskah'
Read the definition and Ibn Abidin's explanation. Understand that it involves a payment to a tenant for vacating leased property, and the name indicates a strong right of possession.
This is a specific Hanafi issue related to lease and occupancy rights.
3
Recognize the second treatise on waqf
The treatise 'Ladhhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'' deals with the validity of endowing undivided shares. Al-Maydani refers readers to it for deeper insight.
This shows the breadth of his legal writings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
نفسه، في (۱۲) صفحة، عند حفيد المؤلف في دمشق. كما توجد ثلاث نسخ خطية منها في مكتبة الظاهرية بدمشق، برقم (٤٧٩٣ ، ٦٥٦٢، ٨٢٠٦).
وقد شرح هذه الرسالة نجل المؤلف الشيخ إسماعيل بـن عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني (1)
وقد ذكر المؤلفُ في هذه الرسالة فرائض الدين وواجباتـه علـى عامة المؤمنين، وبين فيها ما جاء في حديث جبريل عليه السلام، مـن الإيمان والإسلام والإحسان، فكتب مختصراً شديداً في علــم التوحيد، وآخر في أحكام العبادات من الطهارة والصلاة والزكاة والصوم والحج، ثم خَتَمَ الرسالة بخاتمة ذَكَرَ فيها أسبابَ حُسن الخاتمة، من تقوى الله، ومراقبته وخشيته مع الحث على الإكثار من ذكر الله، وما يُقرب إليه جل وعلا.
وهكذا فهي إسعافات أولية لا بد منها للمبتدىء، ولا يَسَعُ الجهل بها، مفيدة جداً للناشئة المباركة، ممن يحرص على تعلم أمور دينه.
والرسالة قيد الطبع بتحقيق كاتب هذه الحروف، أسأل الله أن يتمم بالخير، مع الإخلاص والقبول والعافية.
(۱) حلية البشر ٨٦٨/٢.

Chapter One: Biography of the erudite scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It itself, in 12 pages, with the author's grandson in Damascus. There are also three manuscript copies in the Zahiriyya Library in Damascus, numbers (4793, 6562, 8206). The author's son, Sheikh Ismail bin Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maydani, has commented on this treatise. (1) The author mentioned in this treatise the obligatory duties of religion upon all believers, and explained in it what came in the hadith of Jibril, peace be upon him, of faith, Islam, and ihsan. So he wrote a very concise work on the science of tawhid, and another on the rulings of acts of worship: purification, prayer, zakat, fasting, and pilgrimage. Then he concluded the treatise with a conclusion in which he mentioned the causes of a good end, such as taqwa of Allah, watching Him, and fearing Him, along with urging the increase of dhikr of Allah and what brings one closer to Him, the Exalted. Thus, these are essential provisions necessary for the beginner, and ignorance of them is not permissible, very beneficial for the blessed youth who are keen to learn the matters of their religion. The treatise is under publication with the verification of the writer of these letters. I ask Allah to complete it with good, sincerity, acceptance, and well-being. (1) Hilyat al-Bashar 2/868.

Chapter One: Biography of the erudite scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. 'Mushadd al-Maskah' (1) - A treatise on. Topic of Mashadd al-Maskah: It concerns the vacancy and vacating of shops, premises, and leased land, whereby the tenant occupying the shop or land is given an agreed amount of money in exchange for vacating it and leaving it for a new tenant. The erudite scholar Ibn Abidin discussed it in his Hashiya, and said regarding the reason for naming this issue with this name: It is called 'Maska' because its holder has a grip on it such that it cannot be taken from his hand because of it. It is also called 'Mashadd al-Maskah' because 'al-mashadd' comes from 'al-shidda', meaning strength, i.e., the strength of holding on. End quote. I have not found a copy of it. 9 - Ladhhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'. Al-Maydani himself mentioned it in al-Lubab (3) by this name, and said: 'Whoever desires more insight should refer to our treatise: Ladhhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'.' End quote. (ε) Al-Baytar (4) mentioned it and said: 'He has a treatise on the validity of waqf of undivided shares.' End quote. (1) Al-Baytar mentioned it in Hilyat al-Bashar 2/868. (2) 4/17 (Bulaq ed.). (3) 2/182. (4) Hilyat al-Bashar 2/868.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction by the editor (or compiler) presenting the life and works of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab. It first describes a treatise authored by al-Maydani that covers the fundamentals of faith (tawhid) and the rulings of worship (purification, prayer, zakat, fasting, pilgrimage), based on the famous hadith of Jibril. The editor notes that this treatise is essential for beginners and has been commented upon by the author's son. The passage also lists two additional works by al-Maydani: 'Mashadd al-Maskah' (a treatise on the compensation given to a tenant for vacating leased property) and 'Ladhhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'' (on the ruling of waqf of undivided shares). The former is discussed by Ibn Abidin, who explains the etymology of 'Maska' as a firm grip to protect the right of possession. This passage thus provides valuable bibliographic information and context for understanding al-Maydani's scholarly output within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
مَشَدَّ المَسْكَة (Mashadd al-Maskah): A term referring to a payment given by a new tenant to the existing occupant of a leased property (shop, premises, land) in exchange for vacating it. The name implies a strong grip or tenacity, indicating that the occupant has a right that cannot be easily revoked.
المَسْكَة (al-Maskah): Derived from the root meaning 'to hold' or 'to grip'; in this context it refers to the right of possession or occupancy that gives the holder a firm entitlement to compensation.
الخُلُوِّ والفراغية (al-khuluw wal-firaghiyyah): The act of vacating or leaving a leased property. In Hanafi law, this concept is associated with the practice of 'mashadd al-maskah' where an outgoing tenant receives payment for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Maydani's treatises provide essential Hanafi rulings on both worship and property rights, with 'Mashadd al-Maskah' illustrating the school's recognition of customary practices in lease contracts.
