Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's Treatises: A Bibliographical Overview
Biographical introduction listing the author's treatises

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four treatises of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani mentioned in the passage and state the legal subject of each.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's treatises address specific real-world issues like tenant rights, joint endowment, and property partition.

This biographical passage from al-Lubab introduces Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's own works beyond his main commentary. Understanding these treatises shows how later Hanafi scholars produced targeted writings on practical legal problems, from vacating leased property to dividing common shares. The passage also cites earlier authorities like Ibn Abidin and al-Baytar, grounding al-Maydani's contributions in the broader Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first treatise
Locate the treatise 'Mashadd al-Maskah' and read its description. Note that it deals with khuluww—the practice of paying a tenant to vacate leased premises.
The passage explains the naming as 'strength of adherence' because the tenant has a firm grip on the property.
2
Identify the second treatise
Find 'Ladhdhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'' and note its subject: the ruling on endowing undivided shares (musha'). Al-Maydani refers readers to this treatise for deeper investigation.
Al-Baytar describes it as a treatise on the validity of waqf musha'.
3
Identify the third treatise
Find the untitled 'Risalah fi al-Qismah' (Treatise on Division). The passage says it was prompted by a fatwa incident where partners divided property and one suffered excessive harm.
The manuscript is preserved in al-Zahiriyya, Damascus, in the author's handwriting.
4
Identify the fourth treatise
Note the brief mention of a treatise on usul al-fiqh. The text is cut off, but it shows al-Maydani also wrote on principles of jurisprudence.
This treatise is not described further in the passage.
5
Recognize scholarly context
Observe how al-Maydani references Ibn Abidin and al-Baytar. This demonstrates that his treatises engage with earlier Hanafi scholarship and contribute to ongoing debates.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
10 - Treatise on Division (al-Qismah).
Al-Maydani himself mentioned it in al-Lubab (1) without naming it, in the Book of Division, when discussing the dispute of the dividers (mutqasimun), saying: "Whoever desires complete attainment in this matter, let him refer to our treatise, for we have discussed it thoroughly."
It is a treatise concerning a fatwa incident that occurred among some virtuous people, the description of which is: "Partners divided the common property by means of a divider appointed by the judge, then it became evident to one of them that there was excessive (fahish) harm in his share..."
Its beginning: "Praise be to Allah, the Bestower, the Guide to the paths of righteousness...", and after that: "The servant ... Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani says... This is a treatise which the incident of fatwa prompted to be written..."
Its end: "It was completed (taswid) on Tuesday, five nights into the sacred month of Rajab of the year 1259... written by its compiler Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi..."
This copy, in the author's handwriting, is preserved in al-Zahiriyya in Damascus, number (7079), in five folios.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section listing the works of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab. The text first describes his treatise "Mashadd al-Maskah" on the issue of khuluww (vacating leased properties) and its naming. It then mentions three more treatises: "Ladhdhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'" (on joint waqf), a treatise on division (al-qismah) concerning a fatwa incident, and another on usul al-fiqh. The author provides details about each work, including references to scholars like Ibn Abidin and al-Baytar, and notes manuscript locations. This biographical entry serves as front matter, indicating the scholarly contributions of al-Maydani beyond his main commentary on al-Quduri.

Key Terms
مَشَدَّ المَسكَة (Mashadd al-Maskah): A treatise on the legal ruling of paying money to vacate a leased property, also known as khuluww.
لَذَّة الأسماع في حكم وَقْف المشاع (Ladhdhat al-Asma' fi Hukm Waqf al-Musha'): A treatise on the ruling of waqf (endowment) of undivided shares (musha').
رسالة في القسمة (Risalah fi al-Qismah): A treatise on the division of jointly owned property, addressing a specific fatwa incident where one partner suffered loss.

Biography of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and His Notable Works in Hanafi Fiqh
Biographical introduction listing the author's own works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the titles and subjects of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani’s treatises and explain their relevance to Hanafi fiqh and usul.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar’s works reflect the breadth of fiqh—from property division to defending the faith.

This lesson introduces you to the author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and his own treatises mentioned in his biography. Knowing the author's broader scholarly output helps contextualize his main commentary and gives insight into practical issues he addressed. The passage lists four works covering the division of property, a usul al-fiqh clarification, the grave issue of insulting Islam, and a refutation of a doubt. As you read, focus on identifying each treatise's subject, the legal terms used (e.g., ghabn fahish, qassam, sabb), and the author's motivation for writing them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his main work
Note that the author is Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. His full name and scholarly lineage appear in the biographical part of the passage. The treatises listed are his own separate works, some written in response to real fatwa incidents.
The passage is from the beginning of al-Lubab, where the author often refers readers to his own treatises for more detail.
2
List the four treatises and their subjects
Read the descriptions of each treatise: (10) on division (qisma) involving ghabn fahish, (11) clarifying a point in Usul al-Fiqh from Manar al-Anwar, (12) on punishing those who insult Islam (sabb), and (13) refuting a doubt. Note the title of each and the key issue it addresses.
The numbering (10-13) indicates the author's list continues from earlier entries not shown here.
3
Understand key legal terms
The passage introduces three important Hanafi terms: al-ghabn al-fāḥish (gross defect), al-qassām (official divider), and al-sabb (insulting). Define each and recall their legal consequences in Hanafi law: ghabn fahish can void a contract, qassam is appointed by a judge, sabb leads to apostasy.
These terms are explained in the key terms section below.
4
Analyze the motivation behind each treatise
For each work, determine why al-Maydani wrote it. The treatise on division was prompted by a real fatwa incident. The usul treatise clarifies a specific point. The work on insulting Islam addresses a common social problem. The refutation was for a doubt of some scholars. This shows his practical engagement with contemporary issues.
The author's choice of the word 'al-ḥusām' (cutting sword) in title 12 indicates a stern stance.
5
Relate the treatises to broader Hanafi scholarship
Place each treatise within Hanafi disciplines: the division work is furu' (transactions), the usul work is methodology, the insult work involves kufr and ridda, the refutation likely touches on theology or fiqh. This demonstrates the author's expertise across multiple fields.
Manar al-Anwar is a famous Hanafi usul text by Imam al-Nasafi, showing al-Maydani's engagement with that tradition.

First Chapter: Biography of the learned Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani

10 - A treatise on division (al-qisma). Al-Maydani himself mentioned it in al-Lubab (1), and did not name it, that is in the Book of Division, when discussing the disagreement of the co-dividers. He said: 'Whoever wants to achieve the goal in this topic, let him refer to our treatise, for we have thoroughly discussed it there.' End quote. It is a treatise concerning an incident of fatwa that occurred to some virtuous person, and its form: 'Partners divided the common property among themselves through the direct involvement of a divider from the judge's side, then it became apparent to one of them that there was a gross defect (ghabn fahish) in his share...' Its beginning: 'Praise be to Allah, the Bestower, the Giver, the Guide to the ways of right... After: The servant says... Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani... This is a treatise prompted by an incident of fatwa...' Its end: 'It was written on Tuesday, five nights past of the sacred month of Rajab, the year 1259 AH... by its compiler Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi...' This copy in the author's hand is preserved in al-Zahiriyya in Damascus, number (7079), in five folios.

11 - A treatise clarifying a point in the science of Usul al-Fiqh from the book 'Manar al-Anwar', in the chapter on al-Khas (the specific). The editor of the commentary on al-Tahawiyya by al-Maydani mentioned it for him. (1) The book 'al-Manar' is a useful, well-known summary, and a solid text in Usul al-Fiqh by Imam al-Nasafi, Abdullah ibn Ahmad, died 710 AH, author of 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq' in Hanafi furu', and author of the tafsir. There are many commentaries on 'al-Manar'.

12 - 'Draw the Sword against the Insulter of the Religion of Islam' (2) Al-Bitar mentioned it in Hilyat al-Bashar, and I have not found it. The subject of this book is very important, because it relates to the disbelief of the insulter and his apostasy and his leaving Islam, or his sin and remaining in faith. Especially since many common ruffians frequently curse the religion of Islam with their tongues during their quarrels and anger, and similar things out of ignorance. We ask Allah for safety and well-being. 'al-Husam' is the cutting sword, and thus the author's choice of this word in the title indicates severity in that matter, and Allah knows best.

13 - A treatise refuting a doubt that occurred to some virtuous persons. Al-Bitar mentioned it in Hilyat al-Bashar, but did not mention its subject. (1)
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic section from the beginning of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, where the author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, lists and describes several of his own works. The first work (10) is a treatise on the division of jointly owned property (qisma), written in response to a real fatwa incident involving partners who discovered a defect in their shares. The author refers to it in the main text of al-Lubab as a more detailed resource. The second (11) is a short work clarifying a specific point in Usul al-Fiqh from the well-known text Manar al-Anwar by Imam al-Nasafi. The third (12) is a polemical work titled 'Draw the Sword against the Insulter of the Religion of Islam,' addressing the serious issue of apostasy due to cursing Islam, and emphasizing the severity of such an act. The fourth (13) is a treatise refuting a doubt that occurred to some scholars, though its exact subject is not mentioned by al-Bitar. The passage demonstrates the author's range of interests — from practical fiqh to usul to theological defense — and provides valuable information for researchers about his known writings and their manuscripts.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): A gross defect or deception in a transaction such that one party is significantly disadvantaged, typically based on market value difference.
القسام (al-qassām): An official divider appointed by the judge to oversee the physical division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
السب (al-sabb): Insulting or reviling, especially of Islam or the Prophet, which can lead to apostasy (ridda) in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the subject of the treatise 'Sal al-Husam ala Shātim Din al-Islam'?
A) The division of property among partners
B) The punishment for insulting the religion of Islam and the issue of apostasy
C) A clarification of a point in Usul al-Fiqh
D) A refutation of a doubt about inheritance

Key Takeaway
Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani authored specialized treatises addressing both substantive Hanafi fiqh and usul, reflecting the depth of his scholarship and his responsiveness to contemporary legal issues.

Understanding the Scholarly Output of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani
List of authored works by a Hanafi commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the authored works of Sheikh al-Maidani and explain how a biographical entry (tarjama) aids in assessing a Hanafi text's authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's list of works maps his expertise—morphology, Quranic sciences, fiqh, usul.

This passage introduces the works of the Hanafi commentator Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, the author of the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Instead of a ruling, we encounter a scholarly autobiography—a window into the breadth of a Hanafi master’s contribution. By studying this list, you will learn how biographical notes support textual criticism and tradition authentication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his role
Who is being introduced? Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani is the commentator of 'al-Lubab', a famous Hanafi fiqh text. Note that he himself is listing his own works—a rare self-biographical entry.
This tarjama appears at the beginning of his commentary, establishing his authority.
2
Categorize each work by subject
Go through each mentioned work: 'Sharh Mirah al-Arwah' (sarf/morphology), treatises on 'al-Rasm' (Quranic orthography), 'Isaaf al-Muridin' (fiqh), 'Tuhfat al-Nussak' (fiqh), 'Thabat' (scholarly lineage), and two short usul treatises. This shows his range.
Note that some works are printed, some manuscripts—important for identifying what is available today.
3
Examine the scholarly chain
Look at the references: he cites al-Ayni's early commentary on Mirah, al-Zirikli's remark on the original author's obscurity, and al-Suyuti. These internal references strengthen the biography's reliability.
The mention of al-Ayni's age at his first work (19) adds a human element.
4
Note the method of dating
The author deduces the death date of Husam al-Din from al-Ayni's commentary date (781 AH). This is a common scholarly method—using indirect evidence (qarina) to estimate dates.
Such qara'in are accepted in Hadith and biographical criticism.
5
Reflect on the purpose of the list
The phrase 'هذا ما تيسر لي جمعه' (this is what I managed to collect) shows humility and scholarly caution. He is not claiming completeness, just what he could gather. This honesty is a hallmark of reliable scholarship.
Knowing a scholar's works helps you contextualize his commentary—what other fields did he master?

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani
14 - A commentary on 'Mirah al-Arwah' in the science of morphology.
In 133 pages of medium size, as previously mentioned briefly in the collection that included some of al-Maidani's works, as described by Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah (may Allah have mercy on him), and preserved with al-Maidani's grandson in Damascus.
It is a commentary on the summary 'Mirah al-Arwah' in morphology, by Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Mas'ud Abi al-Fadail Husam al-Din, who died approximately in 700 AH.
It is a beneficial, widely circulated summary that several early imams explained, among them Imam al-Ayni, author of 'al-Binayah'. He named his commentary 'Milahu al-Alwah', completing it in 781 AH at the age of nineteen. It was his first authored work; al-Ayni was born in 762 AH.
Al-Zirikli says in the biography of the author of 'al-Mirah': 'Its author has no known biography, as al-Suyuti said in 'Bughyat al-Wu'at', and al-Badr al-Ayni explained it around 781 AH; from this his death was estimated.' End.
15 and 16 - A treatise on 'al-Rasm', then its commentary.
It was mentioned for him by the author of 'Hilyat al-Bashar'. Perhaps by 'al-Rasm' is meant the orthography of the Noble Quran, and Allah knows best. It is a subject clearly related to the sciences of the Quran.
This is what I have been able to collect of the works of Sheikh al-Maidani. Below I list them all together in alphabetical order to gather them and make them accessible to the gracious observer, with indication of what has been printed and what is manuscript.
1- 'Isaaf al-Muridin fi Iqamat Faraid al-Din' (awaiting publication)
2- 'Tuhfat al-Nussak fi Fadl al-Siwak' (printed)
3- 'Thabat al-Allamah Sheikh Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kuzbari' (d. 1262 AH) (printed)
4- A treatise clarifying a point from the book 'al-Manar' in Usul al-Fiqh, on the topic of 'al-Khas' (manuscript)
5- A treatise refuting a doubt that occurred to some virtuous people (manuscript)
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the works of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, the commentator of 'al-Lubab'. The author lists his own writings. First, he mentions his commentary on 'Mirah al-Arwah' in morphology (sarf), noting its size, the original author (Husam al-Din), and that the commentary by al-Ayni was done at a very young age. He then notes that even the original author's biography is obscure. Next, he mentions two treatises on 'al-Rasm' (likely Quranic orthography) and its commentary. Finally, he provides a numbered list of five of his works: one on establishing the obligations of religion, one on the virtue of the siwak, a scholarly lineage (thabat) of al-Kuzbari, and two short treatises—one on a specific point from al-Manar in usul al-fiqh, and another refuting a doubt. The phrasing 'هذا ما تيسر لي جمعه' indicates humility and scholarly care.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical entry or account of a scholar's life and works.
شرح (sharh): A commentary or exposition on a text, here specifically on 'Mirah al-Arwah'.
مختصر (mukhtasar): A concise summary or abridgment of a larger work, here 'Mirah al-Arwah'.
ثبت (thabat): A scholarly lineage or list of teachers and works, often used for ijazah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A scholar's biographical entry reveals his scholarly network and the range of his contributions, aiding in the evaluation of his fiqh works.

The Works of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
List of works with print/manuscript status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major works of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani and identify the significance of al-Lubab within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani authored over a dozen works, but his commentary on al-Quduri, al-Lubab, remains his most celebrated contribution to Hanafi fiqh.

Before delving into al-Lubab, it is valuable to understand its author—Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani (d. approximately 1290 AH). This biographical passage lists his writings, showing that he was a prolific scholar who produced works on fiqh, usul, Quranic sciences, and refutations. Knowing the breadth of his scholarship helps us appreciate the depth of al-Lubab, which became widely accepted among Hanafi jurists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his significance
Read the passage to note that Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani is the author of al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. His biography is well-known and commented upon by al-Badr al-‘Ayni.
The passage begins with a reference to al-Suyuti and al-‘Ayni.
2
List all works mentioned
Go through the numbered list (1–16) and note each title, whether it is printed (ط) or in manuscript (خ), and its general subject.
Pay attention to the Arabic terms: ط = matbu‘ (printed), خ = makhtut (manuscript).
3
Categorize works by subject
Group the works by field: fiqh (e.g., Is‘af al-Muridin, Ladhdat al-Asma‘, al-Matalib al-Mustataba), usul al-fiqh (e.g., the treatise on al-Khas from al-Manar), aqida (Sharh al-‘Aqida al-Tahawiyya), and other (e.g., Sall al-Husam – a refutation).
This shows the author's range beyond fiqh.
4
Assess the status of al-Lubab
The passage states that al-Lubab is the greatest of his works, granted wide acceptance by Allah. Note it is a commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text.
Al-Lubab is printed and widely studied.
5
Reflect on the other works
Consider that most other works are treatises (rasa’il) on specific issues, many still in manuscript. This indicates that al-Lubab became his magnum opus, while other works addressed niche topics.
The passage ends by noting that these works revolve around fiqh.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of al-Lubab, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. It begins with a note that his biography is well-known (as mentioned by al-Suyuti) and that al-Badr al-‘Ayni wrote a commentary on it around 781 AH, from which his death date is estimated. The text then mentions that some works (treatises on al-Rasm and its commentary) are attributed to him by the author of Hilyat al-Bashar. The main body of the passage is a list of 16 works by al-Maydani, compiled in alphabetical order, with indications of whether each is printed (ط) or in manuscript (خ). Notable among them is 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab', his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi fiqh, which gained wide acceptance. The passage concludes that most of his other works are treatises on specific fiqh issues. This lesson serves as a reference for students to understand the author's scholarly output and the significance of al-Lubab within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biography or biographical entry of a scholar.
رسالة (risala): A treatise or monograph on a specific topic.
شرح (sharh): A commentary or explanation of a text.
مخطوط (makhtut): Manuscript, as opposed to printed (matbu‘).

The Scholarly Legacy of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical overview of a Hanafi polymath's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Maydani’s primary specialization and identify the subject matter of his major works in Hanafi fiqh, usul, creed, hadith, Quranic sciences, and Arabic.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani devoted his life to Hanafi fiqh and authored definitive works spanning usul, creed, hadith, and Arabic.

This biography introduces Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, a towering Hanafi scholar who served as a mufti in Damascus. His writings reveal a deep engagement not only with fiqh but also with usul al-fiqh, theology, hadith criticism, Quranic sciences, and Arabic morphology. Understanding his scholarly output helps us appreciate the breadth expected of a classical Hanafi master.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Primary Specialization
Locate the sentence that states al-Maydani’s main field. The passage begins by identifying him as a Hanafi and notes that he spent his life in fiqh study, teaching, and fatwa. This is the core of his scholarly identity.
All other works build on this fiqh foundation.
2
Catalogue His Works by Discipline
Go through the passage and list each of al-Maydani’s works mentioned. For each, note the subject: usul al-fiqh (al-khass from al-Manar), creed (Sharh al-Tahawiyyah), apostasy rulings (Sull al-Husam), hadith (Kashf al-iltibas and the thabat), Quranic rasm (treatise on rasm), and Arabic morphology (commentary on al-Marah).
This shows the interdisciplinary nature of Hanafi scholarship.
3
Analyze the Purpose of Each Work
For each work, consider why he wrote it. For instance, Kashf al-iltibas defends Imam Abu Hanifa against criticisms in Sahih al-Bukhari. Sull al-Husam addresses apostasy, a fiqh-cum-creed issue. This reveals the practical and polemical contexts.
Many works respond to specific questions or challenges.
4
Synthesize the Range of His Scholarship
Notice that al-Maydani authored in fiqh, usul, creed, hadith, Quranic sciences, and Arabic. This breadth is typical of a senior Hanafi scholar. The passage emphasizes that fiqh was primary, but other sciences supported his juristic work.
The biography praises his dedication and the praise he received from teachers.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
الحنفي، إذ هو تخصصه الذي أفنى عمره في تحصيله وتحريره، وإقرائه وتدريسه مع القيام به في منصب الفتيا بدمشق الشام. كما كان له رسالة لطيفة في مبحث من مباحث علم أصول الفقه الحنفي، وهو مبحث : «الخاص»، من كتاب: «المنار»، في أصول الفقه، للنسفي، جاءت لبيانه وتوضيحه حين سئل عن ذلك. وأما عن علم التوحيد والعقائد، فقد ألف فيه: شرح الطحاوية، ونال به ثناءً عظيماً من مشايخه وأهل العلم والفضل، ولا يخفى أهمية هذا العلم الدقيق. هذا، مع كتابه الآخر : سل الحسام على شاتم دين الإسلام، وموضوع هذا الكتاب فقهي عقدي يتعلق بمسألة مهمة جداً، وهي مسألة الردة، نسأل الله العافية. وأما علم الحديث الذي اشتغل به الميداني اشتغالاً كبيراً، وبخاصة في صحيح البخاري فكان من ثمرة ذلك : كتابه : «كشف الالتباس عما أورده الإمام البخاري على بعض الناس»، لبيان جملة من المسائل الفقهية الفرعية التي نسبت للإمام أبي حنيفة النعمان أيضاً فجاءت هذه الرسالة لبيانها وإزالة إشكال من استشكلها، وهو موضوع ممزوج بالحديث والفقه، يتصل بصحيح الإمام البخاري، وبمذهب أبي حنيفة النعمان عليهما الرحمة والرضوان. ومما كتبه متصلاً بعلم الحديث أيضاً ما جمعه من ثبت لشيخه الكزبري، وهو من وفائه بشيخه، وبره به، وهو كتاب يتعلق بعلم الحديث والأسانيد. وأما علوم القرآن فيغلب على الظن أن رسالته في الرسم، وشرحه عليها، هي في علم رسم القرآن وحروفه، والله أعلم. وهكذا كان للميداني اهتمام أيضاً باللغة العربية وعلومها، وقد دعاه ذلك لشرح كتاب : «المراح» في علم الصرف. وبهذا كله نلحظ أن العلوم التي اهتم بها الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وألف فيها، كان الأول منها هو الفقه الحنفي، وعلم أصول الفقه، وعلم التوحيد والعقائد، وعلوم القرآن، والحديث النبوي الشريف، واللغة العربية. هذا عن العلوم التي ألف فيها، وأما غيرها من العلوم التي اكتسبها وتعلمها، فإن القارئ يلحظ ذلك بشكل واضح من خلال ما كتبه وأشعاره، ونصوص نثره، وقد تقدم بيان ما بثه في مصنفاته ذكره مترجموه ما قرأه على مشايخه من كتب كثيرة في فنون متعددة، بالإضافة إلى مطالعاته الشخصية الخاصة، والله أعلم.
Chapter One: Biography of the Allamah Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The Hanafi, for it is his specialization in which he spent his life studying, revising, teaching, and lecturing, while also serving in the position of fatwa in Damascus. He also had a treatise on a topic of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, namely the topic of 'al-khass' from the book 'al-Manar' in usul al-fiqh by al-Nasafi, which came to explain and clarify it when he was asked about it. As for theology and creed, he authored 'Sharh al-Tahawiyyah' and received great praise from his teachers and people of knowledge and virtue, and the importance of this precise science is not hidden. This, along with his other book 'Sull al-Husam ala Shatim Din al-Islam', whose subject is jurisprudential and creedal, relating to a very important issue, namely apostasy, we ask Allah for well-being. As for hadith, which al-Maydani engaged in extensively, especially Sahih al-Bukhari, one of its fruits was his book 'Kashf al-iltibas amma awradahu al-Imam al-Bukhari ala ba'd al-nas', to explain a number of subsidiary jurisprudential issues attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, and this treatise came to clarify them and remove doubt from those who found them problematic. It is a topic mixing hadith and fiqh, related to Sahih al-Bukhari and the school of Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, may mercy and pleasure be upon them. Also written by him in connection with hadith is what he collected as a thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari, which is part of his loyalty and devotion to his teacher, and it is a book related to hadith and chains of transmission. As for Quranic sciences, it is most likely that his treatise on rasm and his commentary on it are about the science of Quranic orthography and its letters, and Allah knows best. Thus, al-Maydani also had an interest in the Arabic language and its sciences, which led him to write a commentary on the book 'al-Marah' in morphology. Through all this, we note that the sciences that Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani was concerned with and authored in were, foremost, Hanafi fiqh, usul al-fiqh, theology and creed, Quranic sciences, prophetic hadith, and Arabic language. This concerns the sciences in which he authored works. As for other sciences he acquired and learned, the reader can clearly notice that through his writings, poems, and prose texts. His biographers have mentioned what he read with his teachers of many books in various disciplines, in addition to his own personal readings, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It outlines his primary specialization: Hanafi fiqh, in which he dedicated his life to study, teaching, and issuing fatwas in Damascus. The passage then enumerates his key scholarly works. In usul al-fiqh, he wrote a treatise on the topic of 'al-khass' from al-Nasafi's 'al-Manar'. In theology, his 'Sharh al-Tahawiyyah' earned him high praise. He also wrote 'Sull al-Husam' on apostasy, a creedal-legal issue. In hadith, he produced 'Kashf al-iltibas' defending Abu Hanifa against criticisms in Sahih al-Bukhari, and a thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari. In Quranic sciences, he likely wrote on rasm al-mushaf. In Arabic, he commented on 'al-Marah' in morphology. The passage concludes by highlighting that his primary contributions were in Hanafi fiqh, usul al-fiqh, theology, Quranic sciences, hadith, and Arabic.

Key Terms
المنار (al-Manar): A well-known text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi.
شرح الطحاوية (Sharh al-Tahawiyyah): Al-Maydani's commentary on al-Tahawiyyah, a classic Hanafi creedal work.
سل الحسام على شاتم دين الإسلام (Sull al-Husam 'ala Shatim Din al-Islam): Al-Maydani's work on the ruling of apostasy and defending Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Scholarly Profile of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical overview of the scholar's works and poetry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary field of scholarship of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and list the various sciences he authored works in.

Core Idea
Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani was first and foremost a Hanafi jurist, with expertise spanning Quranic sciences, Arabic, hadith, and theology.

This lesson introduces you to the scholarly legacy of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. While his works cover multiple Islamic sciences, the text explicitly states that Hanafi fiqh was the first among his authored fields. Understanding his scholarly profile helps situate his contributions within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his times
Note that Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani is a Hanafi scholar known for his commentary on al-Quduri. His biography is from 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'.
He lived in the 19th century CE (13th century AH).
2
Recognize his primary field
The passage states: 'the first of them was Hanafi jurisprudence'. This establishes fiqh as his core discipline.
This is a key point to avoid confusion with his other works.
3
List his authored sciences
Identify the six sciences he authored in: Hanafi fiqh, usul al-fiqh, tawhid, Quranic sciences, hadith, and Arabic language.
This list shows his breadth as a scholar.
4
Note his additional interests
Observe that he also wrote on Quranic orthography (rasm) and commented on the morphology book al-Mirah, indicating his engagement with Arabic and Quranic sciences.
These works support the primary focus on fiqh.
5
Understand his poetic output
The passage includes his poetry as a fruit of his knowledge, quoting a poem praising his teacher. This reflects the integrated nature of his scholarly and literary contributions.
Poetry was a common medium for scholars to express praise and convey knowledge.

Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. As for the sciences of the Qur’an, it is most likely that his treatise on rasm and his commentary upon it are in the science of Qur’anic orthography and its letters, and Allah knows best. Likewise, al-Maydani also had an interest in the Arabic language and its sciences, and that led him to comment on the book “al-Mirah” on the science of morphology. With all this, we observe that the sciences which Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani was concerned with and authored in, the first of them was Hanafi jurisprudence, and the science of principles of jurisprudence, and the science of tawhid and beliefs, and the Qur’anic sciences, and the noble Prophetic hadith, and the Arabic language. This is regarding the sciences he authored in; as for other sciences that he acquired and learned, the reader clearly observes that through his writings, poetry, prose texts, and the earlier explanation of what he disseminated in his works, his biographers mentioned what he read with his teachers of many books in various arts, in addition to his personal readings, and Allah knows best. The Eighth Section: Poetry of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Among the fruits of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and his intellectual output are many poetic poems, which he composed on specific occasions. About them, the author of Hilyat al-Bashar said: He has poetry and prose that surpass pearls and gems. Among what he composed—and his age at that time was twenty years—is his poem in which he praised his teacher, my master the father, which he began with his saying: By its writer Abd al-Ghani, he praises the dignity of his shaykh and his model, the divine scholar, the spiritual father, by whom the regions boast, my master Shaykh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar, and congratulates him on his safe arrival from the Hijazi journey to his homeland, protected Damascus. May he remain as he wishes. And peace. (1) Hilyat al-Bashar 2/871 (2) 2/868.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a biographical overview of the scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, taken from the first chapter of the book 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'. It begins by noting his works on Qur’anic sciences, specifically a treatise on rasm (Qur’anic orthography) and its commentary, indicating his expertise in this field. His interest in Arabic language led him to write a commentary on the morphology book 'al-Mirah'. The passage then lists the sciences he studied and authored, emphasizing that the foremost of them was Hanafi fiqh, followed by usul al-fiqh, theology, Qur’anic sciences, hadith, and Arabic. This shows his comprehensive mastery and his primary identification as a Hanafi jurist. The biographer then mentions that other sciences he acquired are evident in his writings and poetry. The eighth section of this chapter is dedicated to his poetry, quoting from the biographical dictionary 'Hilyat al-Bashar' that his poetry and prose are excellent. A specific example is given: a poem he composed at age 20 praising his teacher Shaykh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar, congratulating him on his safe return from Hajj. The footnotes reference the source 'Hilyat al-Bashar' volumes and pages.

Key Terms
الرسم (al-rasm): The science of Qur'anic orthography, the writing and spelling of the Qur'an.
المراح (al-Mirah): A well-known book on Arabic morphology (sarf) by Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Mas'ud.
حلية البشر (Hilyat al-Bashar): A biographical dictionary by Muhammad Amin al-Muhibbi, containing biographies of notable figures.

Biography and Poetry of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical introduction and sample poem by the author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the biographical context of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and explain the purpose of the poem in establishing his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's poetry builds credibility and preserves scholarly lineage.

In this lesson, we examine the biographical front matter of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, which introduces the commentator Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The passage includes a poem he composed at age twenty praising his teacher, Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar. Understanding this context helps you appreciate how Hanafi scholars established their authority through literary output and connections to respected teachers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his teacher
Read the heading and first line to find the names: Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (author) and Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar (his teacher). Note the honorific titles used.
Titles like 'al-ʿallāmah' signal high scholarly rank.
2
Locate the poem and its occasion
The passage states the poem was written when the author was twenty years old, upon his teacher's return from a journey to Hijaz. Identify the purpose: praise (madḥ) and congratulations.
Poetry was a common medium for scholarly admiration.
3
Analyze the poetic style
Notice classical Arabic poetic devices: metaphors (lightning, swords, wine), imagery of love and longing. This reflects the author's literary skill.
The references to Hilyat al-Bashar confirm the poem's historical record.
4
Understand the function in a fiqh work
Biographical sections like this establish the commentator's credentials and lineage, reinforcing the reliability of his legal commentary.
In Hanafi tradition, a scholar's biography often precedes his works.

من قد رعى حب القلوب وقد حوى روض الربيع مُعَذِّبَرَ الأرجاء المرتقي رتب الفضائل والعُلا فيها ارتقى للذروة العلياء اللوذعي الألمعي ومـن غــدا علَمَ العلومِ ومَرْجِعَ العلماءِ المفردُ العَلَمُ الذي آثاره دلت عليه بأصدق الأنباء إن قيل مَن هذا الذي تعني فقُلْ: مَن مَدْحه فرض على الشعراء
Chapter One: Biography of the renowned scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Section Eight: Poetry of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Among the fruits of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and his intellectual output are many poetic poems, which he composed on specific occasions. The author of Hilyat al-Bashar said about him: He has poetry and prose that surpass pearls and gems. Among what he composed—and his age then was twenty years—is his poem with which he praised his teacher, my master the father, which he prefaced with his words: Its author, Abd al-Ghani, praises therein the station of his sheikh and his model, the divine scholar, the spiritual father, of whom the regions boast, my master Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar, and congratulates him on his safe arrival from the Hijazi journey to his homeland, protected Damascus. May he remain as he wished. Peace be upon him. (References: Hilyat al-Bashar 2/871, 2/868). A poem in praise of his sheikh, Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, upon his return from the land of Hijaz: And the lightning flashes of the beloved passed in the darkness at dawn, stirring the burning of entrails, and unsheathed the swords of India in their flashing, so the eyes of my tears poured with blood. I only perceived them and I swayed in yearning, like the swaying of the intoxicated with wine. And it healed the heart of the despondent from wasting—excellent medicine after illness. And I thought of a covenant that passed in our direction; may the clouds of weeping water my old covenant. The beloved visited and his light radiated, erasing the darkness of the blackest night. When he appeared, I sang on those hills: the morning tore through the veil of darkness. I kept company with him while longing was between my ribs, kindling the fire of passion and desires. In a night that went mad, its full moon shone, resembling the face of the pasture of the eloquent. And he—who tended the love of hearts and possessed the garden of spring, tormenter [?] of the corners, the one who ascended the ranks of virtues and highness, therein he ascended to the highest peak—the brilliant, the intelligent, and he became the banner of sciences and the reference of scholars, the unique scholar whose traces indicated him with the truest news. If it is said: Who is this that you mean? Then say: One whose praise is an obligation upon poets.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the beginning of the book, introducing the author, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1318 AH/1911 CE), a Hanafi scholar and commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It highlights his intellectual output, particularly his poetry, and presents a full poem composed at age twenty in praise of his teacher, Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar. The poem follows classical Arabic poetic conventions, employing metaphors of lightning, swords, and wine to express longing and admiration. The passage serves as front matter, providing context about the author's scholarly lineage and literary abilities, which is typical in Hanafi works to establish the authority of the commentator. The references cited (Hilyat al-Bashar 2/871, 2/868) indicate the source for this biographical information.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-ʿallāmah): An honorific title meaning 'the most learned scholar' used to denote a person of extensive knowledge, here referring to Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Appreciating the Biographical Introduction in Hanafi Fiqh Works
Biographical preface establishing the author's scholarly credentials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of a biographical introduction (tarjama) in a Hanafi fiqh text and identify the scholarly lineage it establishes.

Core Idea
In Hanafi scholarship, a teacher's praise is the seal of transmitted authority.

This opening chapter is not a legal discussion but a biographical preface—a common feature in classical Hanafi works. The author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, honors his teacher Hasan al-Baytar with a poem, affirming the chain of knowledge transmission. Understanding this front matter helps you appreciate the authority behind the rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the section type
Recognize that this is a tarjama (biography) of the author himself, placed at the beginning of the book.
Look for the heading 'الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني'.
2
Locate the teacher-student relationship
The poem praises Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar; note that al-Maydani is the student.
This establishes the author's direct scholarly lineage.
3
Analyze the poem's imagery
The poem uses classical motifs (lightning, moon, swords) to elevate the teacher's rank.
This is typical in Arabic eulogies to emphasize virtue and knowledge.
4
Connect to Hanafi tradition
Biographical introductions establish ijaza (license) and scholarly lineage, a key feature in Hanafi literature.
They assure readers that the author is trustworthy and connected to the school's authorities.

قصيدة في مدح شيخه الشيخ حسن البيطار حين عودته من بلاد الحجاز
وَمَضَتْ بُرُوقُ الحي في الظلماء سحراً أهاجت لاعجَ الأحشاء ونضت سيوف الهند في إبراقها فَهَمَتْ عيونُ مَدَامِعِي بِدِمَاءِ ما شِمْتُها إلا ومِلْتُ تردُّماً كتمايل النشوان بالصهباء وشَفَتْ فؤادَ المُسْتَهَام من الضَّنَى نِعْمَ الدواء يكون إثر الداء وفكرتُ عهداً قد مضى فَيْناً سقى عهدي القديم به غَمَامُ بكاء زار الحبيب ونـــوره مُتَشَعشع يمحو ظلام الليلة الليلاء لما بدا أنشدت في تلك الربى شق الصباح غلالة الظلماء نادمته والشوق بين جوانحي أذكى لهيب الوجد والأهواء في ليلة جُنَّت فأنور بدرها يحكي مُحَيَّا مَرْتعِ البُلَغَاءِ وَهْوَ من قد رعى حب القلوب وقد حوى روض الربيع مُعَذِّبَرَ الأرجاء المرتقي رتب الفضائل والعُلا فيها ارتقى للذروة العلياء اللوذعي الألمعي ومـن غــدا علَمَ العلومِ ومَرْجِعَ العلماءِ المفردُ العَلَمُ الذي آثاره دلت عليه بأصدق الأنباء إن قيل مَن هذا الذي تعني فقُلْ: مَن مَدْحه فرض على الشعراء
الفاضلُ النَّحْرِيرُ بـدر قـد سَمَا (حَسَنُ) ولكن سيدُ الحُسَنَاء النُّدَمَاءِ (ميدانُنا) بقدومـه قـد فاخرت أمثالهـــا فيـــه مـــع صدر الشريعة والحقيقة والتقى من قلبه كالدرة البيضاء من أتقن المعقول والمنقول واف تخرت به شام على الزوراء مغني اللبيب فكفُّه قَطْرُ النَّدَى ومطولُ التمداح فيه شفائي قد قام في ذكر الإله ملاحظاً بـــــــوابغ الآلاء والنعمـــــــاء الظما بطريقة الصديق قد يروي بخلوص صدقِ ساعةَ الظَّلماء كهف ترى النُّجَباء في أعتابه تأتي لـه بـالنظم والإنشاء لا عيب فيه غير أن نظامه خَلَبَ العقول ببهجة وسَنَاءِ وجميع من في الكون من عُشاقه في الدين والدنيا من السعداء فجعلته بين البرية حليته هو ملجأ الفقراء والغرباء لا زال كالبيت الحرام مُحَرَّماً عند استلام الركن والإيمـاء والعذر لا يخفى فإني مادح يأتي إلى أعتابكم بعنـــاء متخلصاً . بطوه (۱) متشفعاً بالهاشمي وسيد الشفعاء من المجتبى المختارِ مِن كلِّ الملا وهو الذي قد خص بالإسراء
First Chapter: Biography of the venerable scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani

A poem in praise of his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar upon his return from the land of the Hijaz:

The lightning flashes of love appeared in the darkness at dawn, stirring the burning of entrails, and they unsheathed swords of India in their lightning, so the eyes of my tears flowed with blood. I did not perceive them but I leaned in prostration, like the swaying of the intoxicated with wine. It cured the heart of the lovesick from ailment; what an excellent remedy is after illness. I remembered a covenant that passed as pleasure; the clouds of tears watered my old covenant. The beloved visited and his light radiating, erasing the darkness of the blackest night. When he appeared, I chanted in those meadows: 'The morning tore through the veil of darkness.' I kept company with him while longing between my ribs kindled the flame of passion and desires. On a night that was mad, its full moon shone, resembling the face of the pasture of the eloquent.

And he is one who cherished the love of hearts and encompassed the garden of spring, fragrant of the corners, one who ascended the ranks of virtues and highness, therein he rose to the highest peak. The sharp-witted, the brilliant, and he who became the standard of sciences and the refuge of scholars. The singular emblem whose effects pointed to him with the truest news. If it is asked: 'Who is this that you mean?' Say: 'One whose praise is obligatory upon poets.'

The excellent, the incisive, a full moon that rose — Hasan, but the master of beautiful ones. Our Maydani, by his arrival, his likes boasted of him together with the master of Sharia, reality, and piety, his heart like a white pearl. He who mastered the rational and transmitted, and thereby Damascus boasted over Baghdad. The one who enriches the intelligent; his hand is a downpour of dew, and the one who prolongs praise; in him is my healing. He stood observing the sublime blessings and favors. The thirst, by the method of the truthful, he waters with sincere honesty at the hour of darkness. A cave where the nobles are seen at his threshold, coming to him with prose and poetry. No fault in him except that his system captivated minds with joy and radiance. And all who in the universe are his lovers, in religion and world, are among the fortunate. So I made him, among creation, my adornment; he is the refuge of the poor and strangers. May he remain like the Sacred House, sanctified at the touching of the corner and the gesture. And the excuse is not hidden, for I am a praiser coming to your threshold with effort, concluding with slowness (1), interceding through the Hashimi and the master of intercessors, from the chosen, the selected from all mankind, and he who was singled out for the Night Journey.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is the first chapter of the book, which is a biography of the author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. The author includes a poem he composed in praise of his teacher, Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, upon the latter's return from the Hijaz. The poem uses classical Arabic poetic imagery, comparing the teacher's arrival to lightning, swords, and a full moon. It extols the teacher's virtues, knowledge, and high spiritual rank. The author emphasizes that his teacher is the standard of sciences, the refuge of scholars, and that his praise is obligatory upon poets. The poem concludes with the author interceding through the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and referencing the Night Journey (Isra). This biographical section establishes the author's scholarly lineage and his deep respect for his teacher, which is typical in Islamic scholarly works to affirm the chain of transmission and the author's credentials.

Key Terms
عبد الغني الميداني (Abdul Ghani al-Maydani): The author of the commentary 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri', a Hanafi jurist and scholar.
حسن البيطار (Hasan al-Baytar): The teacher of al-Maydani, praised in this poem for his knowledge and virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To provide a legal precedent
B) To honor the author's teacher and establish scholarly credentials
C) To summarize Hanafi fiqh in verse
D) To criticize other madhhabs

Key Takeaway
Biographical introductions in Hanafi fiqh texts are not decoration; they anchor the work in the chain of authoritative transmission.

The Biographical Introduction: Poetry and Prose in a Fiqh Text
Biographical introduction with poetry and prose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of a classical author biography (tarjama) and explain the purpose of including poetry and prose samples within a Hanafi fiqh commentary.

Core Idea
A fiqh author's biography is not idle decoration—it roots his authority in piety and scholarly lineage.

This passage opens al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, a central Hanafi fiqh commentary, with a biography of its author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Instead of diving directly into legal rulings, the text first presents a lengthy poem praising the Prophet and a sample of the author's ornate prose. Understanding why a Hanafi jurist would begin his work this way reveals the deep connection between spiritual devotion and legal authority in our tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the biographical frame
Identify the opening phrase 'الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني' — this signals that the chapter is a biography (tarjama). Tarjama is a standard genre in Islamic scholarly works, providing the reader with the author's credentials and character.
Tarjama is not just a list of facts; it establishes the author's moral and scholarly integrity.
2
Analyze the poem's function
The qasida (poem) is explicitly described as 'في مدح الذات المحمدية' — in praise of the Prophet. Trace the imagery: weeping bird, beloved, intercession. The poem culminates in declaring that without the Prophet, religion would be unknown. This shows the author's deep personal devotion, which qualifies him to comment on sacred law.
Poetry in praise of the Prophet (madih) is a common feature of Islamic scholarship, linking legal knowledge to spiritual love.
3
Examine the prose sample
The passage then presents a sample of al-Maidani's prose from a letter. Note the highly ornate style, use of logical terminology ('مقدمات', 'أشكال', 'عكس', 'طرد') and rhymed prose (saj'). This displays his mastery of Arabic rhetoric, a necessary skill for a faqih and commentator.
Such rhetorical skill was expected of a scholar who would write commentaries and legal opinions.
4
Connect to the Hanafi fiqh context
Consider why al-Maidani (or the editor) placed this biography before the actual fiqh text. It serves to introduce the author as a trustworthy and pious scholar, whose legal interpretations are rooted in both knowledge and righteousness. This is a standard preface in Hanafi works like al-Hidayah and al-Quduri.
The biography builds confidence in the reliability (thiqa) of the transmission.
5
Reflect on your own learning
After reading the poetry and prose, ask: what impression do you have of al-Maidani? Do you feel he is a qualified authority? This is the precise purpose of the tarjama—to prepare the reader's heart and mind for the legal material that follows.
A good biography creates a personal connection to the author.

Chapter One: Biography of the learned scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
A poem in praise of the Muhammadan essence possessing Ahmadian attributes
My eyes poured forth (as) a bird on the willow (tree) warbling, and its heard chirping is piercing to the heart. The vicissitudes of time killed him with separation, so he lamented for his beloved, humbly. So I said to him: O bird, you have cut my heart and you have agitated a lovesick one, while he is in love and... and you reminded me of a day when the heart was cast into affliction, and woe to me, my heart in the passion of love is immersed. So take a narration of the truth of my love, whose chain from me is flowing tears. Indeed my eye caught the glances of a gazelle, with the lightning of her face gleaming in the darkness of hair. Her eyebrow has surpassed in beauty, and her smile is a unique system of jewels. And when she appeared to the lover, she swayed and glanced, so what (is) the moon? what (are) the branches? what (is) the gazelle? (Nothing is) splendid. In her distance, the earth, though vast, is narrow; and in her proximity, the earth, though narrow, is vast. And every lover who is not guided by her beauty is a liar falling into misguidance. To her all beauty is attributed originally, and the beauty of others in creation is derivative.
Until he said (1):
(1) Thus in Hilyat al-Bashar 2/871.
When she advances, the sun prostrates in awe; and when she moves, the branch in the garden is splendid. And I have a deliverance from her aversion by seeking intercession through her, to the one who is my intercessor on the Day of Resurrection. For if not for him, we would not know religion nor piety; and if not for him, no luminary would have existed throughout the ages. And no defect (there is) if it is said: al-Ghanimi is a praiser of the Messenger of God, His servant, in him desiring. So he is a slave of al-Ghani (the Rich), and he has no other than Him when obstacles become severe. This is what I have come across of the poetry of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, and the statement of the author of Hilyat al-Bashar in his biography preceded: 'He has many poems.'
His prose:
*****
And al-Maidani had excellent and innovative prose in addressing his teachers and others. Among his prose: 'What he wrote to my father (1) when he was in the Hijaz in the year 1242 (3): After offering greetings whose universals and particulars conform to the cases of longing, and whose premises affirm the figures that defy description, especially the sketch and definition of yearning, we specify with that the presence of our master, the one of the issue directed to every glory, the burden on the premises of honor deflected from inversion and analogical deduction.'
(1) The speaker is the author of Hilyat al-Bashar 2/870.
(2) Meaning: the age of the prose writer al-Maidani was twenty years.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This is a biographical passage (tarjama) from the opening of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, presenting the life and literary works of the author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The passage begins by identifying the first chapter as a biography. It then presents a long qasida (poem) in praise of the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH), using classical Arabic poetic imagery: the poet weeps, addresses a bird, and uses metaphors of a beloved gazelle to ultimately extol the Prophet's intercession. The poem transitions to direct praise, stating that without the Prophet, religion and piety would be unknown. The author then notes that this is a sample of al-Maidani's poetry, citing the biographical work Hilyat al-Bashar. The second part of the passage displays al-Maidani's prose style: a sample of a letter he wrote to the narrator's father, demonstrating his ornate and complex rhymed prose (saj'). The footnotes clarify that the quotation is from Hilyat al-Bashar and that al-Maidani was twenty years old when he wrote the letter. This passage does not contain legal rulings; it is a literary and biographical introduction to the author.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biography or biographical notice; here, the section of the book dedicated to the author's life.
العلامة (al-Allama): The very learned scholar; a title of respect indicating high scholarly rank.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A classical Hanafi fiqh commentary often begins with a biographical introduction that showcases the author's piety and linguistic skill, reinforcing his authority to interpret the law.

The Scholarly Character of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical account of al-Maydani's poetry and prose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly character of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani as evidenced by his poetry and prose, and explain why his biography is relevant to studying his commentary.

Core Idea
A scholar's poetry and prose reveal both spiritual devotion and intellectual rigor, establishing his authority.

This lesson presents the life and works of the Hanafi commentator Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, whose biography appears in the introduction to his sharh of al-Quduri. The passage includes samples of his poetry praising the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and a letter displaying his mastery of logic and elegant prose. Understanding his scholarly background helps us appreciate the depth and reliability of his commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the biography
The biography (tarjama) is placed at the beginning of the commentary to establish the author's scholarly credentials and chain of knowledge. Note how it blends literary excerpts with factual details.
Biographies in traditional texts serve to authenticate the transmission of knowledge.
2
Examine the poetry sample
Read the Arabic verses and translation. The poem expresses deep love for the Prophet and reliance on him for intercession. What does this reveal about al-Maydani's spiritual state and the purpose of his scholarship?
Poetry was a common medium for expressing tawassul and devotion among Hanafi scholars.
3
Analyze the prose sample
The letter to his father contains logical terms like 'universals', 'particulars', 'subject', and 'predicate'. Identify these terms and consider what they indicate about his intellectual training.
Proficiency in logic (mantiq) was valued in traditional Islamic education, especially in the Hanafi school.
4
Connect to his commentary
How do al-Maydani's poetic sensitivity and logical acumen contribute to the quality of his fiqh commentary? The commentator's personal qualities and broad learning enrich his sharh.
A commentator with adab and 'ilm produces more comprehensive and reliable explanations.
5
Summarize his scholarly qualities
Based on the passage, list the traits that make al-Maydani a trusted authority: piety, eloquence, mastery of logic, and deep respect for his teachers.
These qualities align with the Hanafi tradition of combining knowledge with spiritual refinement.

Biography of the scholar Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. 'If she approaches, the sun prostrates in awe; and if she passes by, the branch in the garden is radiant. I have an escape from her turning away by interceding to her with one who is my intercessor on the Day of Resurrection. Were it not for him, we would not know religion nor piety; were it not for him, there would be no rising throughout time. There is no fault if it is said that al-Ghanimi praises the Messenger of God, His servant, in him is a desiring person. So that one is a slave of al-Ghani, and for him there is none other when obstacles become severe upon him.' This is what I came across of the poetry of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. And the statement of the author of Hilyat al-Bashar in his biography has preceded: 'He has many poems.'
His prose:
*****
* Likewise al-Maydani had elevated and exquisite prose in addressing his teachers and others. Among his prose: 'What he wrote to my father when he was in the Hijaz in the year 1242 AH, after offering greetings whose universals and particulars correspond to the cases of longing, and whose premises establish such forms that the specialist in drawing and definition of longing is incapable of describing. We single out for that the presence of our master, the one possessing the issue directed to every glory, the premises of honor that are excluded from contraposition and conversion. His Excellency our master Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar, may the banner of his virtue never cease to be unfurled in horizons and lands, and may his rank remain accompanied by elevation, and his highest station be carried and placed upon the shoulders of Gemini, and may his enemy be barren of attaining hopes, blameworthy throughout the passage of days and nights... etc.' I say: There has preceded, in the discussion of al-Maydani's character and manners and his fear, what I quoted from his elevated and sublime prose at the end of his commentary on al-Tahawiyyah creed, in his supplications to God Almighty and his hope for forgiveness from Him, and a good end, and winning the gardens.
*****
(1) 'Subject and predicate and all that preceded: logical terms, and their usage in this context indicates breadth of knowledge and literature.' End quote from a gloss on Hilyat al-Bashar 2/870.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the commentary on al-Quduri, presenting the life and works of the Hanafi scholar Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. The author first presents some of al-Maydani's poetry praising the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), demonstrating eloquence and deep devotion. Then he discusses al-Maydani's prose, quoting a letter he wrote to his father while in Hijaz, which employs logical terms like 'universals', 'particulars', 'premises', 'subject', and 'predicate', showing his mastery of logic and refined literary style. The commentator notes that this prose indicates al-Maydani's broad learning. The passage also references al-Maydani's commentary on the Tahawiyyah creed, where his supplications reflect his piety and hope for divine mercy. This biography serves to establish the scholarly authority of al-Maydani, who is the commentator (sharih) of the text being studied.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biography or biographical notice of a scholar.
حلية البشر (Hilyat al-Bashar): A biographical work by al-Muhibbi, cited as a source for al-Maydani's life.
الموضوع والمحمول (al-mawdu' wa al-mahmul): Logical terms: 'subject' and 'predicate' in a proposition, used here to show scholarly depth.
العقيدة الطحاوية (al-'Aqidah al-Tahawiyyah): A famous creedal text by Imam al-Tahawi, upon which al-Maydani wrote a commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Significance of Ijazah in Hanafi Scholarship
Biography and ijazah records of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of ijazah in establishing scholarly authority within the Hanafi tradition and identify its key components as illustrated by Shaykh al-Maydani's biography.

Core Idea
Ijazah is the backbone of scholarly transmission, certifying both knowledge and chain.

Scholarly authority in the Hanafi tradition is not merely a matter of personal study; it is tied to a living chain of transmission (isnad) from teacher to student. This passage from the biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, a prominent Hanafi jurist, shows how ijazah (license) and thabat (compilation of teachers) function as formal attestations of learning. Understanding this practice reveals how fiqh knowledge was preserved and authenticated across generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of ijazah
Read the passage to understand what an ijazah is—a license from a teacher permitting the student to transmit his works or teachings. Note that it is not a mere certificate but a link in the isnad chain.
The term appears twice: al-Maydani gave an ijazah to a student and received ijazat from his teachers.
2
Recognize the role of thabat
The passage mentions al-Maydani compiled a thabat (a list of teachers and chains) for his teacher al-Kuzbari. A thabat serves as a documented record of a scholar's credentials, making the isnad transparent.
Thabat is often written by a student about his own teachers, but here al-Maydani wrote one for his teacher, showing his expertise.
3
Trace how ijazah establishes authority
Notice that when al-Maydani granted an ijazah, he listed his own teachers, thereby transferring the authority of his chain. The recipient could then trace his learning back through al-Maydani to earlier scholars.
The practical effect: the student becomes part of the scholarly lineage.
4
Observe the reliance on senior teachers
Al-Maydani singled out Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar saying 'my greatest benefit was from him.' This shows that not all teachers are equal; the ijazah emphasizes the primary mentor.
Such acknowledgment strengthens the chain's reliability.

Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section presenting the life and scholarly credentials of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, a Hanafi jurist and commentator on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author begins by praising one of al-Maydani's teachers, Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar, using elevated rhymed prose typical of Islamic biographical literature. He notes al-Baytar's virtue and wide reputation. The author then transitions to discuss al-Maydani's character, piety, and his famous work, the commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya, where al-Maydani humbly supplicates to Allah for forgiveness and a good end. A footnote explains that the terms used in the praise are logical terms (mawdu' and mahmul), demonstrating the breadth of the author's knowledge. The second part of the passage (page 124) focuses on the ijazat of Shaykh al-Maydani. It mentions his intensive study of Sahih al-Bukhari and other hadith collections under his teachers, and his compilation of a thabat (a list of his teachers and chains) for his teacher al-Kuzbari. The author states that he found only one documented instance of al-Maydani granting ijaza, which is recorded by the author of Hilyat al-Bashar: al-Maydani gave ijaza to Sayyid Salman Afandi al-Qadiri of Baghdad, listing his teachers and noting that his greatest benefit was from Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar. The author then notes that al-Maydani himself received many ijazat from his teachers, including a full text from Ibn Abidin, and that the praises expressed by his teachers effectively constitute high ijazat. The passage is purely biographical, establishing the scholarly lineage and authority of al-Maydani within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): A license or authorization from a teacher to a student, permitting the student to transmit the teacher's works or teachings.
ثَبَت (thabat): A written compilation listing a scholar's teachers, their chains of transmission, and the works they studied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He wrote a list of his teachers for the requester.
C) He directed the requester to his own teacher Ibn Abidin.
D) He recited a poem praising the requester.

Key Takeaway
Ijazah is not merely a certificate but a formal link in the chain of transmission, preserving the authority of Hanafi fiqh across generations.

The Ijazas of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: Scholarly Authorization
Biographical account of the author's scholarly ijazas and connections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of ijazas in the Hanafi scholarly tradition and identify the key components of an ijaza as illustrated by al-Maidani's example.

Core Idea
An ijaza is the scholarly chain that connects a student to his teachers; al-Maidani's single recorded ijaza reveals the care taken to preserve that chain.

This biographical passage sheds light on the scholarly credentials of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, author of the commentary al-Lubab. It focuses on the ijazas (licenses) he gave and received, emphasizing the importance of chain transmission (isnad) in Islamic scholarship. Understanding ijazas helps us appreciate how Hanafi knowledge was preserved and transmitted through personal teacher-student connections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject and Context
Read the passage and note that it discusses the ijazas of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, his engagement with hadith books, and his compilation of a thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari.
The context is the author's scholarly activity within the Hanafi tradition.
2
Extract Information on Ijazas Given by al-Maidani
Find the part that mentions the only recorded ijaza he gave: to al-Sayyid Salman Afandi al-Qadiri, the naqib of Baghdad. Notice that al-Maidani listed his teachers in that ijaza.
The passage says it is 'most likely' he gave many ijazas, but only one is recorded.
3
Analyze the Content of the Recorded Ijaza
Examine what al-Maidani wrote in that ijaza: he named his teachers and particularly highlighted his teacher Hasan al-Baytar. This shows the chain of transmission.
The ijaza serves as a document linking the recipient to the scholar's teachers.
4
Understand the Role of Thabat and Teacher Links
Note that al-Maidani compiled a thabat for his teacher al-Kuzbari, listing his own chains and teachers. This is a common practice to preserve scholarly lineage.
A thabat is a record that strengthens the authenticity of transmitted knowledge.
5
Examine the Colophon's Significance
The passage ends with a colophon from the manuscript, indicating the completion of the book by al-Maidani himself. It includes the date and his name, serving as a mark of authenticity.
Colophons are important for dating manuscripts and verifying authorship.

Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Ninth Section
Ijazas of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani to Others
There has already been an explanation of the great engagement of Sheikh Abdul Ghani with Sahih al-Bukhari and his reading of it multiple times to his teachers, and his engagement with the six hadith books and others. As previously mentioned, he compiled a thabat (list of chains) for his teacher al-Kuzbari, and mentioned his chains and teachers. Based on this, it is most likely that Sheikh al-Maidani had many ijazas for his students and those seeking ijaza, but I have only come across mention of one ijaza, which the author of Hilyat al-Bashar mentioned, where he said:
(1)
... al-Maidani read under my father, Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, and he used to praise him greatly in the presence of high and low. When the respected al-Sayyid Salman Afandi al-Qadiri, the naqib of Baghdad, requested an ijaza from him, he wrote for him the names of his notable teachers. When he mentioned my father, he said: 'My greatest benefit was from him.' End quote.
As for the ijazas of his teachers to him, the text of the ijaza of his teacher Ibn Abidin has already been mentioned in full, as has my transmission of the many high praises of him from his teachers—praises that include the highest ijazas from them.

Peace be upon Jesus son of Mary, and the completion of this book was achieved by the grace of Allah and His guidance at the hands of the most humble of servants and the most needy of the intercession of the master of servants, Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. May his Lord grant him his hopes. Mid-Sha'ban al-Mu'azzam, [place unclear], and ... from all ... the Supreme Master, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and ...

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from the editor/researcher, discussing the ijazas (scholastic licenses) of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It first notes his extensive study of Sahih al-Bukhari and other hadith collections under various teachers, and his compilation of a thabat (a work listing his teachers and chains of transmission) for his own teacher al-Kuzbari. The editor then observes that although al-Maidani likely gave many ijazas to students, only one is recorded: the one he granted to al-Sayyid Salman Afandi al-Qadiri, the naqib of Baghdad. In that ijaza, al-Maidani listed his teachers, emphasizing his teacher Hasan al-Baytar. The passage also references previously mentioned ijazas from his teachers to him, particularly the full text of Ibn Abidin's ijaza. The remainder of the text appears to be a colophon from the manuscript, noting the completion of the book by al-Maidani himself, with some unclear words possibly indicating the place and date. This section serves to establish the author's scholarly authority and transmission credentials.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): A license or authorization given by a scholar to another person to transmit a particular book or body of knowledge, indicating that the recipient has studied the work with the granting scholar and is permitted to teach or narrate it.
ثَبَت (thabat): A work compiled by a scholar listing his teachers, the books he studied with them, and his chains of transmission (isnad). It serves as a record of scholarly lineage and authorization.
مستجيز (mustajīz): A person who requests an ijaza from a scholar, seeking authorization to transmit the scholar's works or knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ijazas preserve the scholarly chain of transmission, and even a single recorded ijaza from a scholar like al-Maidani offers valuable insight into his teachers and teaching network.

The Library of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: A Legacy of Hanafi Knowledge
Biographical account of library acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the transfer of Ibn Abidin's library to al-Maidani and identify the key individuals involved in preserving this collection.

Core Idea
A scholar's library is a treasure of knowledge; al-Maidani's acquisition of Ibn Abidin's library preserved a vital Hanafi heritage.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri presents a biographical account of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and the remarkable library he acquired. The narrative underscores how scholarly works and collections are passed down through teacher-student relationships, ensuring the continuity of the Hanafi tradition. Understanding this transmission helps us appreciate the chain of authority in our fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the origin of the library
Read the first part: who originally collected the library, and for how long? Note that it was Ibn Abidin who amassed it over many years.
Ibn Abidin is the famous Hanafi jurist and author of Radd al-Muhtar.
2
Trace the transfer to al-Maidani
After Ibn Abidin's death, what happened? Why did al-Maidani decide to buy most of the library? Look for his motive of loyalty and preservation.
Al-Maidani's action prevented the library from being scattered among merchants.
3
Identify the other buyer
Who bought the remainder? Find the name of the other student of Ibn Abidin mentioned.
Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar also purchased part of the library.
4
Understand the fate of the library
What eventually happened to the portion with al-Maidani? What does the narration from Abu al-Yusr Abidin tell us about later efforts to gather the collection?
The library was largely destroyed by fire during the French bombardment of Damascus.
