الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
المبحث العاشر
مكتبة الشيخ الميداني
من المعلوم أن وجود مكتبة كبيرة نفيسة متخصصة لدى العالم المتيقظ النابه المنبه ، مما يزيد في تقدمه العلمي، ونشاطه وبـروزه، وتحقيقه وتدقيقه، ويكون لذلك الأثر الكبير في تميزه على غيره، كما يكسب مؤلفاته مزايا علمية خاصة لا تجدها عند غيره، وفوائد أخرى كثيرة غير هذا.
وإن مما أكرم الله تعالى به العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أن رزقه الله تعالى مكتبة جامعة قيّمة نفيسة غنية نادرة متميزة، حَوَتْ كتباً كثيرة، وفي فنون متنوعة، وبخاصة في المذهب الحنفي.
هذه المكتبة عَمِلَ على جَمْعها سنين طويلة شيخه العلامة ابن عابدين صاحب الحاشية المشهورة، ثم آل معظمها إلى تلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وذلك حين أراد ورثةُ ابن عابدين بيعها، فكان من وفاء الميداني الشيخه وبره بأستاذه، أنه لم يرض بتفريط الورثة بتلك المكتبة العظيمة، وضياعها شَذَرَ مَذَرَ بأيدي التجار المشترين ، فاشترى غالبها ، والقسم الآخر اشتراه تلميذ ابن عابدين الآخر الشيخ محمد البيطار نجل الشيخ حسن البيطار.
وقد ذكر خبر ما تقدم من بيع وشراء مكتبة ابن عابدين : الدكتور الشيخ محمد عبد اللطيف صالح الفرفور، حيث قال :
-
(حدثني شيخنا الدكتور أبو اليسر عابدين ـ ابن العلامة مفتي الشام الشيخ محمد أبو الخير عابدين بن أحمد بن عبد الغني بن عمر ـ وكانت ولادة أبي اليسر سنة ١٣٠٧هـ، ووفاته سنة ١٤٠١هـ، قال الشيخ أبو اليسر :
«لما توفي ابن عابدين صاحب الحاشية، وكان ابنه السيد علاء الدين صغيراً دون البلوغ في الثامنة من عمره، فجاء تلاميذ ابـن عابدين فابتاعوا مكتبته كلها، بما فيها مصنفاته، وأكثرها عند الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في حي الميدان، ووصل منها شيء للشيخ محمد البيطار ) ، وقرأ - علاء الدين - على الميداني المذكور. اهـ
وقد جَمَعَ أكثرها فيما بعد - ولا سيما المخطوطات - المرحوم الشيخ أبو الخير عابدين، والدكتور الشيخ أبو اليسر رحمه الله، حتى كادت تتكامل، وعنده زيادات لم تُطبع ، وما بقي عند الشيخ عبد الغني ذهب حريقاً حينما قصف الإفرنسيون الميدان بالمدفعية).
(۱) ابن عابدين وأثره في الفقه الإسلامي (۳۱۷/۱، ١٠١٦/۲، ١١٠١.
(۲) محمد ابن الشيخ حسن بن إبراهيم البيطار ممن لازم ابن عابدين صاحب الحاشية ملازمة تامة، واستنسخ جميع مؤلفاته في حياته، وكان أمين الفتوى في دمشق، المولود سنة ۱۲۳۱هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ۱۳۱۲هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى، وتقدم أنه تلاميذ الميداني، له ترجمة في تاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر ١١٩/١. من
Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Tenth Section: The Library of Sheikh al-Maidani
It is well-known that the presence of a large, precious, specialized library for a vigilant, distinguished, and alert scholar increases his scientific progress, activity, prominence, verification, and precision. It has a great impact on his distinction from others, and it gives his writings special scientific merits not found in others, as well as many other benefits beyond this.
Indeed, among the honors that Allah Almighty bestowed upon the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was that He granted him a comprehensive, valuable, precious, rich, rare, and distinguished library. It contained many books on various arts, especially in the Hanafi school.
This library was collected over many long years by his teacher, the scholar Ibn Abidin, author of the famous commentary (Hashiya). Then most of it passed to his student Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani when Ibn Abidin's heirs wanted to sell it. Out of al-Maidani's loyalty and devotion to his teacher, he did not consent to the heirs squandering that great library and its being scattered left and right in the hands of merchant buyers. So he bought most of it. The other part was bought by another student of Ibn Abidin, Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar, son of Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar.
The news of the sale and purchase of Ibn Abidin's library was mentioned by Dr. Sheikh Muhammad Abd al-Latif Salih al-Farfur, who said:
- (My teacher, Dr. Abu al-Yusr Abidin – son of the scholar Mufti of Sham, Sheikh Muhammad Abu al-Khayr Abidin ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Ghani ibn Umar – and the birth of Abu al-Yusr was in 1307 AH, and his death was in 1401 AH, said Sheikh Abu al-Yusr: 
'When Ibn Abidin, author of the Hashiya, died, his son Sayyid Ala al-Din was a minor under the age of puberty at eight years old. So the students of Ibn Abidin came and bought his entire library, including his writings. Most of it is with Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani in the al-Maidan district, and some of it reached Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar. And Ala al-Din studied under the aforementioned al-Maidani. End quote.
Afterward, most of it—especially the manuscripts—was gathered by the late Sheikh Abu al-Khayr Abidin and Dr. Sheikh Abu al-Yusr, may Allah have mercy on them, until it almost became complete. He had additions that were not printed. What remained with Sheikh Abdul Ghani was destroyed by fire when the French bombarded al-Maidan with artillery.)
(1) Ibn Abidin and His Influence on Islamic Jurisprudence (1/317, 2/1016, 1101).
(2) Muhammad ibn Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Bitar was one who closely followed Ibn Abidin, author of the Hashiya, and copied all his writings during his lifetime. He was the trustee of fatwa in Damascus, born in 1231 AH and died in 1312 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He is mentioned earlier among the students of al-Maidani. His biography is in the History of Scholars of Damascus in the Fourteenth Century, 1/119.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, specifically Chapter One on the translation (biography) of the commentator Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The author highlights the importance of a scholar's library in enhancing his scientific output and distinction. He describes how Allah blessed al-Maidani with a comprehensive library, which originally belonged to his teacher, the renowned Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin (author of the well-known Hashiya 'Radd al-Muhtar'). After Ibn Abidin's death, his heirs wanted to sell the library. Out of loyalty and respect, al-Maidani purchased most of it to prevent its dispersal. The remainder was bought by another student, Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar. The passage then cites Dr. Muhammad Abd al-Latif al-Farfur, who relays a narration from Dr. Abu al-Yusr Abidin (a descendant of Ibn Abidin) confirming the purchase. The narration also notes that Ibn Abidin's young son, Ala al-Din, later studied under al-Maidani. Subsequently, al-Maidani's portion of the library was lost in a fire during the French bombardment of Damascus. This account illustrates the deep scholarly bonds and the care for preserving Islamic knowledge within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
مكتبة (maktabah): A collection of books, specifically the valuable library originally owned by Ibn Abidin and later acquired by al-Maidani.
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): The famous Hanafi jurist Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Abidin (d. 1252 AH), author of the authoritative Hashiya 'Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar'.
الميداني (al-Maidani): Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani (d. 1298 AH), the Hanafi scholar and commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who originally collected the library that later came to al-Maidani?
A) Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani himself
B) Ibn Abidin (the author of the Hashiya)
C) Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar
D) Dr. Abu al-Yusr Abidin

Key Takeaway
The transfer of Ibn Abidin's library to al-Maidani exemplifies the Hanafi tradition of preserving and transmitting scholarly legacy through teacher-student relationships.

Preservation of Ibn Abidin's Scholarly Legacy
Relates the purchase and collection of Ibn Abidin's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the transmission of Ibn Abidin's library and identify the key figures involved in its preservation.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's students purchased his entire library after his death, preserving his works for future Hanafi scholarship.

This passage recounts the fate of the library of the great Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin after his death. It highlights the efforts of his students and later scholars to preserve his works, most notably al-Maydani, who collected the majority. Understanding this transmission is important for appreciating the continuity of Hanafi learning in Damascus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central event
Determine what happened to Ibn Abidin's library immediately after his death.
The key fact is that his students purchased the entire library.
2
Trace the first account
Follow the account from Dr. al-Farfur, noting where the books ended up.
Most went to al-Maydani, some to al-Bitar.
3
Trace the second account
Examine the account from Dr. al-Hafiz and note any differences or confirmations.
It confirms al-Maydani's collection and adds details about his son Ismail.
4
Note the subsequent fate
What happened to al-Maydani's portion and how was the rest of the library reassembled?
Al-Maydani's portion was destroyed by French fire; later descendants recollected most works.
5
Reflect on significance
Why does this chain of custody matter for Hanafi fiqh?
It ensures the authoritative transmission of Ibn Abidin's works, central to later Hanafi jurisprudence.

وقد ذكر خبر ما تقدم من بيع وشراء مكتبة ابن عابدين : الدكتور الشيخ محمد عبد اللطيف صالح الفرفور، حيث قال : (حدثني شيخنا الدكتور أبو اليسر عابدين ـ ابن العلامة مفتي الشام الشيخ محمد أبو الخير عابدين بن أحمد بن عبد الغني بن عمر ـ وكانت ولادة أبي اليسر سنة ١٣٠٧هـ، ووفاته سنة ١٤٠١هـ، قال الشيخ أبو اليسر : «لما توفي ابن عابدين صاحب الحاشية، وكان ابنه السيد علاء الدين صغيراً دون البلوغ في الثامنة من عمره، فجاء تلاميذ ابـن عابدين فابتاعوا مكتبته كلها، بما فيها مصنفاته، وأكثرها عند الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في حي الميدان، ووصل منها شيء للشيخ محمد البيطار ) ، وقرأ - علاء الدين - على الميداني المذكور. اهـ وقد جَمَعَ أكثرها فيما بعد - ولا سيما المخطوطات - المرحوم الشيخ أبو الخير عابدين، والدكتور الشيخ أبو اليسر رحمه الله، حتى كادت تتكامل، وعنده زيادات لم تُطبع ، وما بقي عند الشيخ عبد الغني ذهب حريقاً حينما قصف الإفرنسيون الميدان بالمدفعية). اهـ من كلام الدكتور الفرفور. كما جاء هذا الخبر من طريق أخرى عن الشيخ الدكتور أبي اليسر عابدين، وهو ما ذكره محقق «شرح العقيدة الطحاوية»(۱) للميداني : الدكتور محمد مطيع الحافظ، فقد قال: ذكر لنا شيخنا العلامة أبو اليسر عابدين حفظه الله تعالى، أن كتب ومؤلفات العلامة ابن عابدين، قد جمع أكثرها العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني بعد وفاة شيخه ابن عابدين، وانتقلت من بعده إلى ابنه الشيخ إسماعيل، ومما يؤسف له، أن كثيراً منها قد فقد حريق أصابها من قبل الإفرنسيين زمن الانتداب». اهـ
And the news of what preceded of the sale and purchase of Ibn Abidin's library was mentioned by Dr. Sheikh Muhammad Abd al-Latif Salih al-Farfur, who said: My teacher, Dr. Abu al-Yusr Abidin – son of the scholar, the Mufti of Sham, Sheikh Muhammad Abu al-Khayr Abidin bin Ahmad bin Abd al-Ghani bin Umar – and Abu al-Yusr was born in 1307 AH and died in 1401 AH. Sheikh Abu al-Yusr said: 'When Ibn Abidin, the author of the Hashiya, died, and his son Sayyid Ala al-Din was a young boy under the age of puberty at eight years old, then the students of Ibn Abidin came and bought his entire library, including his writings. Most of it was with Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani in the al-Maydan district, and some of it reached Sheikh Muhammad al-Bitar. And Ala al-Din studied under the mentioned al-Maydani. End. And later, most of it – particularly the manuscripts – was collected by the late Sheikh Abu al-Khayr Abidin and Dr. Sheikh Abu al-Yusr, may Allah have mercy on them, until it nearly became complete. He has additions that have not been printed. And what remained with Sheikh Abd al-Ghani was destroyed by fire when the French bombed al-Maydan with artillery.' End quote from Dr. al-Farfur. And this news also came from another chain from Dr. Sheikh Abu al-Yusr Abidin, as mentioned by the editor of 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya' by al-Maydani, Dr. Muhammad Muti' al-Hafiz, who said: Our teacher, the scholar Abu al-Yusr Abidin – may Allah preserve him – told us that the books and writings of the scholar Ibn Abidin were mostly collected by the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani after the death of his teacher Ibn Abidin, and after him they were transferred to his son Sheikh Ismail. And regrettably, many of them were lost due to a fire that struck them from the French during the mandate period.' End.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing what happened to the library of the great Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin (the author of Radd al-Muhtar) after his death. Two accounts are given, both ultimately quoting Abu al-Yusr Abidin, a descendant. The first account, from Dr. al-Farfur, explains that Ibn Abidin's students purchased the entire library to preserve it, and most of it went to Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (the author of al-Lubab), with some reaching Muhammad al-Bitar. The young son of Ibn Abidin, Ala al-Din, later studied under al-Maydani. Subsequently, most of the collection was reassembled by later descendants, though al-Maydani's portion was destroyed in a French bombardment. The second account, from Dr. Muhammad Muti' al-Hafiz, confirms that al-Maydani collected the bulk of Ibn Abidin's works, and the collection later passed to his son Ismail, with much lost to fire during the French mandate. This background is important for understanding the transmission of Ibn Abidin's scholarly legacy and the chain of Hanafi authority in Damascus.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Shami, the renowned Hanafi jurist, author of Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar (d. 1252 AH/1836 CE).
الميداني (al-Maydani): Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH/1881 CE), a Hanafi scholar from Damascus, author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab (a commentary on al-Quduri).
علاء الدين (Ala al-Din): Sayyid Ala al-Din ibn Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin, the young son of Ibn Abidin who later studied under al-Maydani.
أبو اليسر عابدين (Abu al-Yusr Abidin): Dr. Muhammad Abu al-Yusr Abidin (b. 1307 AH, d. 1401 AH), a descendant of Ibn Abidin and a scholar who helped recollect the library.
محمد البطار (Muhammad al-Bitar): A Hanafi scholar from Damascus who received some of Ibn Abidin's works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) His students

D) Sheikh al-Maydani alone

Key Takeaway
The preservation of Ibn Abidin's library by his students and later scholars ensured the continuity of Hanafi legal tradition in Damascus.

The Making of a Scholar's Library: Ibn Abidin's Bibliographic Legacy
Biographical description of Ibn Abidin's library and its origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Abidin's personal library and his father's support shaped his scholarly output in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A scholar's library is the workshop of his mind—Ibn Abidin's father built the shelves; he filled them.

This passage offers a rare glimpse into the material foundation of great scholarship. Ibn Abidin, the towering Hanafi jurist of the Ottoman era, did not work in isolation—his father's generous support allowed him to amass a library of rare and comprehensive works, many in his own hand. Understanding this background helps us appreciate the depth and breadth of his commentaries, especially the Radd al-Muhtar.

Guided Path
1
Locate the narrator and the subject
Identify who is speaking (Dr. Muhammad Abd al-Latif al-Farfur) and about whom (Ibn Abidin). This frames the rest of the passage.
The passage is transmitted through al-Maydani's work, showing the chain of preservation.
2
Note the unique quality of the library
Observe the phrase 'the like of which had never been collected'—this indicates the extraordinary comprehensiveness of Ibn Abidin's collection across all sciences.
Many books were in his own handwriting, showing active copying and study.
3
Identify the cause: his father's role
The passage explicitly states that his father bought every book he wanted and paid for it. This financial and moral support was the key enabler.
His father's words reveal that he saw his son as reviving the scholarly tradition he himself had lost.
4
Extract the father's motivation
The father says: 'you have revived what I have lost of the way of my predecessors.' This shows that the father valued his son's scholarship as a continuation of the Salaf's path.
This connects to the Hanafi emphasis on preserving and transmitting the madhhab's foundational works.
5
Reflect on the significance for Hanafi fiqh
Ibn Abidin's library enabled him to cite many sources, reconcile conflicting positions, and produce the comprehensive Radd al-Muhtar, which remains a central reference in Hanafi fatwa.
The library is not just a personal collection but a tool for the entire madhhab.

وصف مكتبة العلامة ابن عابدين التي آلت للشيخ الميداني: قال الدكتور محمد عبد اللطيف الفرفور : وكانت عند ابن عابدين كتب من سائر العلوم، لم يُجمع على منوالها، وكان كثير منها بخط يده، وكان السبب في جمعه هذه الكتب عديمة النظير والده، فإنه كان يشتري له كل كتاب أراده، ويقـول لـه : اشتر ما بدا لك من الكتب، وأنا أدفع لك الثمن، فإنك أحييت ما أمتُه أنا من سيرة سلفي، فجزاك الله خيراً يا ولدي
Description of the library of the scholar Ibn Abidin which came to Sheikh al-Maydani: Dr. Muhammad Abd al-Latif al-Farfur said: Ibn Abidin had books from all sciences, the like of which had never been collected, and many of them were in his own handwriting. The reason for his collection of these unparalleled books was his father, for he would buy for him every book he wanted, and would say to him: 'Buy whatever books you desire, and I will pay the price for you, for you have revived what I have lost of the way of my predecessors. May Allah reward you well, my son.'
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a biographical description detailing the nature and origin of Ibn Abidin's library. Ibn Abidin, the great Hanafi jurist, possessed a comprehensive collection of books spanning all Islamic sciences, many in his own hand. The key factor in building this library was his father's generous and encouraging support. His father urged him to buy any book he wanted and promised to pay, seeing his son's dedication as a revival of the scholarly tradition of the early Muslims. This background situates Ibn Abidin's scholarly output within the context of a rich personal library, which later was preserved by al-Maydani as noted in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Shami, the renowned Hanafi jurist, author of Radd al-Muhtar (d. 1252 AH/1836 CE).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He was a wealthy merchant
D) He copied all books by hand

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abidin's unparalleled library, built with his father's support, was the material foundation for his monumental contributions to Hanafi fiqh.

The Role of Book Collection in Hanafi Scholarship: Al-Maidani and Ibn Abidin's Library
Biographical account of library acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how al-Maidani's acquisition of Ibn Abidin's library contributed to the preservation and transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Book collection and preservation are essential for the continuity of the Hanafi madhhab.

This biographical passage from 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' recounts how Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, a prominent Hanafi scholar, acquired the priceless library of his teacher Ibn Abidin. Understanding this history reveals the vital role that dedicated scholars and patrons played in ensuring that core Hanafi texts survived and remained accessible for future generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures
Locate the names Ibn Abidin, al-Maidani, and Ibn Abidin's father. Note their relationships: teacher-student, father-son.
Ibn Abidin is the great Hanafi jurist; al-Maidani is his student who wrote a famous commentary on al-Quduri.
2
Trace the library's origin and growth
Read how Ibn Abidin's father financed the collection, buying every requested book regardless of cost. Recognize the father's role as a patron, not a scholar.
The father's statement 'you have revived what I had let die' shows he valued scholarship.
3
Follow the transmission chain
After Ibn Abidin's death, al-Maidani collected most of the books. They later passed to al-Maidani's son. Note the disruption: a fire during the French mandate destroyed many works.
This illustrates the fragility of manuscript collections and the importance of preservation.
4
Assess the impact on al-Maidani's scholarship
Al-Maidani acquired the library at age thirty and used it for 46 years. The text says he 'surpassed his peers' due to this resource and his own efforts.
This shows how access to primary sources elevated a scholar's authority.
5
Extract the lesson for the Hanafi school
Consider how the library's contents—comprehensive Hanafi manuscripts—enabled al-Maidani to produce his commentary and preserve the school's heritage.
The passage underscores that textual continuity depends on both creation and curation.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
اهـ من كلام الدكتور الفرفور.
كما جاء هذا الخبر من طريق أخرى عن الشيخ الدكتور أبي اليسر عابدين، وهو ما ذكره محقق «شرح العقيدة الطحاوية»(١) للميداني : الدكتور محمد مطيع الحافظ، فقد قال:
ذكر لنا شيخنا العلامة أبو اليسر عابدين حفظه الله تعالى، أن كتب ومؤلفات العلامة ابن عابدين، قد جمع أكثرها العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني بعد وفاة شيخه ابن عابدين، وانتقلت من بعده إلى وابنه الشيخ إسماعيل، ومما يؤسف له، أن كثيراً منها قد فقد بسبب حريق أصابها من قبل الإفرنسيين زمن الانتداب». اهـ
وصف مكتبة العلامة ابن عابدين التي آلت للشيخ الميداني:
(٢) قال الدكتور محمد عبد اللطيف الفرفور :
وكانت عند ابن عابدين كتب من سائر العلوم، لم يُجمع على منوالها، وكان كثير منها بخط يده، وكان السبب في جمعه هذه الكتب عديمة النظير والده، فإنه كان يشتري له كل كتاب أراده، ويقول له : اشتر ما بدا لك من الكتب، وأنا أدفع لك الثمن، فإنك أحييت ما أمتُه أنا من سيرة سلفي، فجزاك الله خيراً يا ولدي
وأعطاه أبوه كُتُب أسلافه الموجودة عنده من أثرهم، الموقوفة على ذراريهم وكان والده تاجراً عابداً صالحاً». اهـ
وقال العلامة الفقيه الشيخ مصطفى الزرقا في تقريظه لكتاب: «ابن عابدين وأثره في الفقه الإسلامي» (١):
.... إن ما تـوافر لابن عابدين من وسائل الإحاطة بكتب المذهب، إلى جانب ذكائه وذاكرته وخبرته العميقة في المراجعة عن المسائل، لم يتوافر مثله فيما يبدو لأحد قبله، فقد كان والده غنياً موسراً، فكان يأتيه بالكتب المرجعية وكلها مخطوطة بخطوط مختلفة من مختلف البلاد الإسلامية مهما كان ثمن الكتاب، على صعوبة هذه المواصلات والبحث في ذلك العهد، فما توافر لديه من كتب المذهب بخاصة، لا يتوافر مثلها في المكتبات العامة والخاصة، ....». اهـ
هكذا كان عظيم حال مكتبة العلامة ابن عابدين التي آل غالبها للشيخ الميداني، فحفظها واستفاد منها ما يقرب من ست وأربعين سنة إلى سنة وفاته رحمه الله تعالى.
وكانت سنه يوم شرائه لها في الثلاثين، وقد بلغ كمال النضج العلمي، مع ما آتاه الله من جد ونشاط علمي، وذكاء وصلاح، حتى فاق أقرانه ومعاصريه.
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. End of the words of Dr. al-Farfur. This report also came from another chain from Sheikh Dr. Abi al-Yusr Abidin, as mentioned by the editor of 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya' by al-Maidani: Dr. Muhammad Muti al-Hafiz, who said: Our teacher, the eminent scholar Abu al-Yusr Abidin, may Allah protect him, mentioned to us that the books and works of the eminent scholar Ibn Abidin were mostly collected by the eminent scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani after the death of his teacher Ibn Abidin, and then they passed from him to his son Sheikh Isma'il. Unfortunately, many of them were lost due to a fire caused by the French during the mandate period. End of quote. Description of the library of the eminent scholar Ibn Abidin that came to Sheikh al-Maidani: (2) Dr. Muhammad Abd al-Latif al-Farfur said: Ibn Abidin had books from all sciences, unmatched in collection; many were in his own handwriting. The reason for his collecting these unparalleled books was his father, who would buy him every book he desired and say to him: 'Buy whatever books you want, and I will pay the price, for you have revived what I had let die from the path of my predecessors. May Allah reward you well, my son.' And his father gave him the books of his ancestors that he had, which were endowed to their descendants. His father was a merchant, a devout worshiper and righteous man. End of quote. The eminent jurist Sheikh Mustafa al-Zarqa said in his praise of the book 'Ibn Abidin and His Impact on Islamic Jurisprudence' (1): '... What Ibn Abidin had of means to encompass the books of the school, along with his intelligence, memory, and deep experience in reviewing issues, was not available, as it seems, to anyone before him. His father was rich and wealthy, so he brought him reference books, all manuscripts in different handwritings, from various Islamic countries, regardless of the cost of the book, despite the difficulty of these communications and research in that era. What he had of books of the school in particular is not found in public or private libraries...' End of quote. Thus was the magnificent state of the library of Ibn Abidin, most of which came to Sheikh al-Maidani. He preserved it and benefited from it for nearly forty-six years until the year of his death, may Allah have mercy on him. He was thirty years old on the day he purchased it, and he had reached full scientific maturity, with what Allah had given him of effort and scientific activity, intelligence and righteousness, until he surpassed his peers and contemporaries.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction of 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maidani, describing the acquisition of Ibn Abidin's library. The text highlights the generosity of Ibn Abidin's father, who spared no expense to build an unparalleled collection of Hanafi reference works. After Ibn Abidin's death, al-Maidani—his student—collected most of these works and preserved them. Unfortunately, a fire during the French mandate destroyed many of these treasures. Al-Maidani purchased the library at age thirty and used it for 46 years, which contributed to his becoming the leading Hanafi scholar of his time. This passage underscores the importance of book collection and preservation in Islamic scholarship, especially for the Hanafi madhhab. Al-Maidani's dedication ensured that future generations could access the foundational texts of the school.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): The great Hanafi jurist Muhammad Amin ibn Abidin (d. 1252 AH/1836 CE), author of the famous super-commentary 'Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar'.
الميداني (al-Maidani): Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani (d. 1298 AH/1881 CE), Hanafi scholar and author of 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab', a commentary on Al-Quduri's mukhtasar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He donated his own books from his trade.
B) He bought every book Ibn Abidin wanted, regardless of cost.
C) He wrote books himself.
D) He inherited them from ancestors.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maidani's purchase of Ibn Abidin's library at age 30 allowed him to surpass his contemporaries and preserve Hanafi scholarship for future generations.

Al-Maydani's Acquisition of Ibn Abidin's Library
Biography of a Hanafi scholar and his acquisition of a major library

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of Ibn Abidin's library for the Hanafi school and identify how al-Maydani's acquisition of it contributed to his scholarly output.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's access to Ibn Abidin's unmatched library enabled his authoritative commentary on Al-Quduri.

This passage is a biographical sketch, not a legal ruling. It highlights the scholarly resources that allowed al-Maydani to write Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. Understanding this background helps you appreciate the authority of his commentary within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject and His Relationship to Ibn Abidin
Read the first part of the passage. Who is being introduced? How is he connected to Ibn Abidin? Note that al-Maydani is the student or inheritor of Ibn Abidin's library.
The passage is from a chapter on al-Maydani's biography.
2
Summarize the Description of Ibn Abidin's Library
Focus on Mustafa al-Zarqa's taqriz. What made Ibn Abidin's library unique? Identify key phrases: 'manuscripts from various Islamic lands', 'regardless of price', 'unparalleled in public and private libraries'.
This shows the depth of resources available to Ibn Abidin.
3
Explain How Al-Maydani Acquired the Library
Find where the passage states that the majority of Ibn Abidin's library passed to al-Maydani. Note his age at acquisition (thirty) and how long he used it (nearly forty-six years).
This demonstrates the long period of scholarly benefit.
4
Describe the Outcome of His Scholarship
Understand that al-Maydani's access to this library enabled him to produce his major work, Al-Lubab. The passage emphasizes his excellence over contemporaries due to his resources and diligence.
The library was a direct factor in his scholarly success.
5
Note the Current Unknown Fate of the Library
The passage ends by stating that the library's current location is unknown despite efforts to trace it. Reflect on the fragility of scholarly heritage.
This adds a historical note of loss.

Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. 129. And his father gave him the books of his predecessors that were with him, from their legacy, endowed to their descendants. Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It focuses on his acquisition of the large library of the famous Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin. The passage quotes Sheikh Mustafa al-Zarqa, who describes the comprehensive nature of Ibn Abidin's collection, which included manuscripts from various Islamic lands, made possible by his wealthy father. This library was unparalleled in its time. Upon Ibn Abidin's death, the majority of this library came into the possession of al-Maydani, who preserved it and continued to benefit from it for nearly half a century until his own death. The passage ends by noting that the current whereabouts and status of that library are unknown, despite efforts to trace it through al-Maydani's descendants. This biography explains the scholarly resources that al-Maydani had access to, which greatly enhanced his ability to write his commentary, Al-Lubab.

Key Terms
الميداني (Al-Maydani): Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the Hanafi scholar who wrote Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri.
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin, a leading Hanafi jurist and author of Radd al-Muhtar, the major reference for later Hanafi fatwa.
تقريظ (taqriz): A commendation or praise of a book, often written by a scholar to endorse its contents.

The Scientific Activity of Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical account of scholarly habits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the four key aspects of al-Maidani's scientific activity and explain how they exemplify the ideal Hanafi scholar's approach to knowledge.

Core Idea
A scholar's diligence is shown through eagerness to learn, service to teachers, collecting books, and spreading knowledge.

This passage introduces us to the scholarly character of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. By examining his scientific activity, we learn the values that shaped a great Hanafi jurist and how his dedication serves as a model for students of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and focus
The passage centers on the life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, specifically his scientific activity. Note the transition from a note about his library to the main discussion.
The library note sets context; the main focus is the four points that follow.
2
List the four points of scientific activity
The text enumerates four aspects: (1) keen attendance at scholarly circles and constant presence with teachers, (2) devotion and service to teachers, (3) love of books and collecting a rare library, (4) active teaching and spreading knowledge to elite and common people.
Each point reflects a distinct dimension of scholarly life.
3
Understand the significance in the Hanafi tradition
These activities align with the Hanafi emphasis on direct transmission from teachers (talaqqi), respect for mashayikh, preservation of texts, and community education.
Service to teachers (khidma) is a hallmark of traditional learning.
4
Reflect on how these qualities contribute to scholarly authority
Al-Maidani's diligence earned him the description 'devoted to serving Sharia and teaching sciences,' which legitimizes his role as a commentator and authority in the Hanafi school.
Biographical accounts establish the reliability of a scholar's transmission.

Chapter Eleven: His Scientific Activity. It appears through examining the life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and the praises of his teachers and mentors that he was from his childhood, the beginning of his seeking knowledge, active and diligent, and he continued in that with progress and increase until the end of his life. His scientific activity can be highlighted in the following points: 1- His extreme eagerness to attend the circles of knowledge with his teachers, and his rare constant attendance with them. 2- His devotion to his teachers, his dedication in serving them and pleasing them, and fulfilling their rights and duties. 3- His intense love for books, and his collection of a rare, extensive, and diverse library. 4- His activity in delivering multiple lessons, spreading knowledge, and benefiting the elite and the common people. And in the description of his biographers it came: 'He was devoted to serving the Sharia and teaching the sciences.' Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, focusing on his scientific activity. The text begins with a note about the author's library, mentioning that nothing is known about what remains of it, despite the author's efforts to track it. Then it proceeds to describe the sheikh's academic diligence, emphasizing that he was active from childhood and continued throughout his life. His activity is summarized in four points: first, his keenness to attend scholarly gatherings and his rare continuous presence with his teachers; second, his devotion and service to his teachers, fulfilling their rights; third, his love for books and collecting a rare, diverse library; fourth, his activity in teaching multiple lessons and spreading knowledge for the benefit of both the elite and the common people. Finally, the biographers describe him as being devoted to serving the Sharia and teaching the sciences. This biography shows the author's high level of commitment and contribution to the Hanafi tradition through teaching and writing.

Key Terms
مكتبة (maktaba): The library that al-Maidani collected, described as rare, extensive, and diverse.
مشايخ (mashayikh): The teachers of al-Maidani, to whom he was devoted and whom he served.

The Scholarly Activity of Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical narration of a Hanafi scholar's life and work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key aspects of Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's scholarly activity and explain why his biography is relevant to the authority of his fiqh commentary.

Core Idea
A scholar's meticulous activity and piety establish the reliability of his fiqh work.

This biographical sketch of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, from the introduction to his renowned commentary *Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri*, highlights the habits that built his authority. Understanding his dedication to seeking knowledge, teaching, and issuing fatwas gives us confidence in his commentary. This lesson walks you through the eight points of his scholarly activity and their significance for Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight points of scholarly activity
The passage lists eight numbered aspects of al-Maidani's work. Read through each one and note the core idea: eagerness for learning, service to teachers, love for books, teaching, authorship, ifta, asceticism, and travels.
These points are not just biographical trivia; they are the foundation of his scholarly authority.
2
Connect each point to its impact on fiqh scholarship
For each point, ask: How does this contribute to the reliability of his fiqh commentary? For example, his dedicating to teachers ensures he received authentic transmission; his authorship and ifta show his practical engagement with fiqh.
The passage explicitly states his main teaching was in Hanafi fiqh and its principles.
3
Recognize the specific example of teaching al-Shifa
The text notes that he taught *al-Shifa* by Qadi Iyad twice during a Hajj journey. This shows his dedication even while traveling, and his expertise in multiple sciences beyond fiqh.
This example illustrates the depth of his scholarly commitment.
4
Understand the authority of the author for his commentary
By establishing al-Maidani's rigorous scholarly life, the biography strengthens the trustworthiness of *Al-Lubab* as a Hanafi reference. A student relying on his commentary can be confident in its accuracy.
This is why biographical introductions are common in classical works.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

المبحث الحادي عشر
نشاطه العلمي

يظهر من خلال الوقوف على حياة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني وثناءات مشايخه وأساتذته عليه أنه كان منذ صغره، وبداية طلبه للعلم نشيطاً مُجداً، واستمر على ذلك مع تقدم وازدياد إلى آخر حياته، ويمكن إبراز نشاطه العلمي في النقاط التالية :
۱- حرصه الشديد على حضور مجالس العلم عند شيوخه، وملازمته النادرة لهم.
۲ بره بمشايخه، وتفانيه في خدمتهم وإرضائهم، والقيام بحقوقهم وواجباتهم.
- حُبُّه الشديد للكتب، وجمعه لمكتبة نادرة واسعة متنوعة.
٤- نشاطه في إلقاء الدروس المتعددة، ونشره للعلم، ونفع الخاصة والعامة، وقد جاء في وصف مترجميه: «أنه كان معتكفاً على خدمة الشريعة، وتدريس العلوم (۱)
(1) ينظر كلام تلميذه الذي سعى بطباعة اللباب في مقدمة النسخة المطبوعة في اسطنبول سنة ١٢٧٥هـ.

وكانت أبرز دروسه في دمشق في الفقه الحنفي وأصوله، مـع تدريسه لفنون أخرى.
ومن نشاطه العلمي في هذا المجال أنه أقرأ كتاب «الشفا» للقاضي عياض مرتين وهو مسافر في المدينة المنورة، حين قدم حاجاً سنة ١٢٨٠هـ، كما سيأتي في رحلاته، وهذا خبر وصــلنـا عنـه فـي ذلك، وما لم يصل هو أكثر، والله أعلم، إذ هذا النشاط الأصل في حياة العلماء أمثال الميداني.
ه نشاطه في التأليف والتحقيق في مسائل العلم في فنون متعددة.
-٦- تسلُّمه منصب الإفتاء (۱) ، وانشغاله الكبير به مع خاصة النـاس وعامتهم.
-٧- بعده عن الدنيا ومشاغلها، وزهده فيها.
رحلاته المتعددة إلى بلاد الحجاز للحج والعمرة، ولقيـاه علماء الحرمين الشريفين، وغيرهم من علماء العالم الإسلامي، وتبادله العلوم معهم أخذاً وإعطاء.
كما رحل إلى مصر والتقى بعلماء مصر، وعلماء العالم الإسلامي الذين حضروا حفل افتتاح قناة السويس.
(۱) «ابن عابدين وأثره في الفقه الإسلامي ۹۸۷/۲ ، نقلا عن ترجمة الشيخ محمد علاء الدين لوالده العلامة ابن عابدين
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Eleventh Topic: His scholarly activity. It appears from examining the life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and the praises of his teachers and professors upon him that he was, from his childhood and the beginning of his pursuit of knowledge, active and diligent, and he continued thus with progress and increase until the end of his life. His scholarly activity can be highlighted in the following points: 1. His extreme eagerness to attend the study circles of his teachers and his rare dedication to them. 2. His devotion to his teachers, his self-sacrifice in serving them and pleasing them, and fulfilling their rights and duties. 3. His intense love for books and his collection of a rare, extensive, and diverse library. 4. His activity in delivering multiple lessons, spreading knowledge, and benefiting the elite and the common people. It is described by his biographers: 'He was devoted to serving the Sharia and teaching the sciences.' (1) See the words of his student who sought to print al-Lubab in the introduction of the edition printed in Istanbul in 1275 AH. His most prominent lessons in Damascus were in Hanafi fiqh and its principles, along with his teaching of other arts. Among his scholarly activities in this field is that he taught the book 'al-Shifa' by Qadi Iyad twice while traveling in Medina when he came for Hajj in 1280 AH, as will come in his travels. This news reached us about that, and what did not reach us is greater, and Allah knows best, for this activity is the norm in the lives of scholars like al-Maidani. 5. His activity in authorship and verification of scholarly issues in various arts. 6. His assumption of the position of ifta', and his great preoccupation with it for the elite and common people. 7. His distance from the world and its concerns, and his asceticism in it. His multiple travels to the land of Hijaz for Hajj and Umrah, and his meetings with scholars of the two Holy Sanctuaries, and other scholars of the Islamic world, and his exchange of knowledge with them give and take. He also traveled to Egypt and met with scholars of Egypt and scholars of the Islamic world who attended the opening ceremony of the Suez Canal. (1) 'Ibn Abidin and his influence on Islamic jurisprudence' 2/987, quoting from the biography of Sheikh Muhammad Ala al-Din for his father, the scholar Ibn Abidin.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the introduction of 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The author presents the 'scholarly activity' of al-Maidani in a series of points. The passage opens by stating that from his youth he was active and diligent in seeking knowledge, and this continued throughout his life. The first point highlights his dedication to attending his teachers' study circles. The second notes his respectful service to his teachers. Third, his love for books and collecting a rare library demonstrates his scholarly investment. Fourth, his teaching and spread of knowledge, both to the elite and masses, and it is mentioned that he was described as devoted to serving Sharia and teaching. The text then specifies that his main teaching in Damascus was in Hanafi fiqh and its principles, along with other sciences. A specific example is given: he taught 'al-Shifa' by Qadi Iyad twice while on a Hajj journey in Medina. The passage then lists further activities: authorship and verification in multiple fields; his assumption of the position of ifta (issuing fatwas); his asceticism and distance from worldly concerns; and his travels to Hijaz and Egypt, meeting scholars and exchanging knowledge. The biography serves to establish the authoritativeness of al-Maidani as a Hanafi scholar, and his work 'al-Lubab' is a standard commentary on al-Quduri's matn. The Hanafi student should appreciate that the author's scholarly credentials are part of why his commentary is relied upon.

Key Terms
الإفتاء (al-ifta): The position or act of issuing formal legal opinions (fatwas). Al-Maidani assumed this role, indicating his authority in Hanafi fiqh.
الشفا (al-Shifa): A famous work by Qadi Iyad al-Maliki on the virtues of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Al-Maidani taught this text, showing his breadth of knowledge beyond fiqh.
اللباب (al-Lubab): Al-Maidani's commentary on *Al-Quduri*, a foundational Hanafi text. The title means 'The Core'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Medina
C) Damascus
D) Egypt

Key Takeaway
The scholarly activity of Abdul Ghani al-Maidani—his dedication to teachers, teaching, authorship, ifta, and asceticism—establishes the authority of his commentary *Al-Lubab* in Hanafi fiqh.

Life and Contribution of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical sketch of a Hanafi scholar-mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and identify his key contributions to Hanafi fiqh, including his appointment as mufti.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography illuminates the context and authority behind his fiqh works.

Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani is the author of Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, a key Hanafi commentary. His life story—his teaching, travels, and role as a mufti—provides important background for understanding his legal methodology. This lesson introduces his scholarly profile so you can better situate his fiqh rulings and commentary.

Guided Path
1
Locate the scholar in Hanafi history
Identify who Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani is: a 19th-century Hanafi scholar, author of Al-Lubab. Note his place in the line of Hanafi commentators.
2
Identify his main scholarly activities
From the text, list his teaching of Hanafi fiqh and usul, his authorship, and his role as mufti. Understand that each activity contributes to the weight of his opinions.
3
Examine his travels and scholarly exchanges
He traveled to Hijaz and Egypt, meeting scholars and teaching. This shows his access to diverse knowledge networks, enriching his fiqh perspectives.
4
Relate his biography to his fiqh work
His asceticism, worship, and charity reflect the ethical dimension expected of a mufti. These personal qualities are integral to the authority of his fatwas and commentary.

Understanding Author Biography in Hanafi Scholarship
Biographical account of scholarly activities and journeys

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of a tarjama in a Hanafi matn and identify three elements from Shaykh al-Maydani's biography that establish his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's tarjama is the chain of trust — knowledge is authenticated through the life and connections of its bearer.

This passage presents the biography (tarjama) of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of al-Quduri. In the Hanafi tradition, a tarjama is not mere background; it establishes the author's reliability, his practical application of knowledge, and his place in the scholarly network. Understanding this helps you appreciate why his commentary is authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the tarjama
Read the first sentence and note that the biography is placed before the main text. Consider: why would a Hanafi work include this? What does it tell you about the author's authority?
In Hanafi texts, the tarjama often includes the author's teachers, students, travels, and righteous deeds, linking the text to a living tradition.
2
Extract the practical application of knowledge
In section 9, find the phrase 'ثمرة العلم وهو العمل' (the fruit of knowledge is action). List the specific actions mentioned: acts of worship, dhikr, building mosques, feeding the poor. How do these actions support his authority?
Hanafi scholarship emphasizes that true knowledge leads to righteous action (al-ilm al-nafi).
3
Analyze the scholarly travels and connections
Read the travel section. Identify the three main destinations (Damascus, Egypt, Hijaz) and the scholars he met (al-Watari, al-Hadrawi, Prince Abdul Qadir). What do these connections reveal about his scholarly network?
Travel for knowledge (rihla) is a hallmark of classical Islamic scholarship, ensuring transmission across regions.
4
Assess the significance of teaching Al-Shifa
The text mentions he taught 'Al-Shifa' by Qadi Iyad in Medina twice. Why is this notable? What does it imply about his expertise?
Al-Shifa is a major work on the Prophet's status; teaching it in Medina indicates high recognition.
5
Synthesize the tarjama's contribution to authority
Combine what you learned: a scholar with practical piety, extensive travel, and recognition from peers is a reliable transmitter. How does this affect your trust in his commentary on al-Quduri?
The tarjama functions as a scholarly pedigree, enhancing the credibility of the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
٩- نشاطه في ثمرة العلم، وهو العمل، ومن ذلك قيامه بأنواع العبادات والنوافل، وكثرة ذكره لربه جل وعلا، وبناؤه للمساجد والعناية بها وإطعام الفقراء والمساكين وغير هذا مما وفقه الله إليـه بفضله سبحانه.

المبحث الثاني عشر
رحلات الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
كانت للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني عدة رحلات من دمشق، فقد سافر إلى بلاد الحجاز مكة المكرمة والمدينة المنورة عدة مرات للحج والعمرة.
إحداها كانت سنة ١٢٨٠هـ ، وقد أقرأ في هذه الرحلة بالمدينة المنورة كتاب «الشفا للقاضي عياض» مرتين، وممن سمعـه عليه في المرتين المحدث الشيخ علي بن ظاهر الوَتَرِي المدني (١٢٦١ هـ ـ ١٣٢٢هـ)، كما ذكر هذا العلامة السيد جعفر بن إدريس الكتاني(١) (١٢٤٦ هـ ـ ١٣٢٣هـ)، حيث يروي «الشفا» من طريق الوتري. وفي سنة ١٢٨١هـ اجتمع به في مكة المكرمة العلامة المؤرخ الشيخ أحمد الحضراوي المكي، كما ذكر هذا في كتابه: نزهة الفكر (٢)
وهكذا رحل من دمشق إلى بلاد مصر، ومنها إلى الحجاز، وكان عُمره آنذاك أربعة وستين عاماً، في رحلة كانت مع الأمير عبد القادر
(١) في فهرست مشايخه ص ٢١٦ ط: دار ابن حزم، بیروت).
.٢( ١٧٦/٢)
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
9- His activity in the fruit of knowledge, which is action, including his performance of various acts of worship and supererogatory prayers, his abundant remembrance of his Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, his building and caring for mosques, feeding the poor and needy, and other such deeds to which Allah guided him by His grace.

Twelfth Section
The Travels of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani undertook several journeys from Damascus. He traveled to the lands of Hijaz, Mecca and Medina, multiple times for Hajj and Umrah.
One of these was in the year 1280 AH. During this journey, he taught in Medina the book “Al-Shifa by Qadi Iyad” twice. Among those who heard it from him on both occasions was the muhaddith Shaykh Ali ibn Zahir al-Watari al-Madani (1261 AH – 1322 AH), as mentioned by the scholar Sayyid Ja'far ibn Idris al-Kattani (1246 AH – 1323 AH), who narrates “Al-Shifa” through al-Watari. In the year 1281 AH, the historian scholar Shaykh Ahmad al-Hadrawi al-Makki met him in Mecca, as he mentioned in his book “Nuzhat al-Fikr” (2).
Thus he traveled from Damascus to Egypt, and from there to Hijaz, and at that time he was sixty-four years old, in a journey with Prince Abdul Qadir.
(1) In his Fihrist Mashayikh, p. 216, Dar Ibn Hazm, Beirut.
(2) 176/2
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the life and travels of Shaykh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, a Hanafi scholar and commentator of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The first part (section 9) describes his practical application of knowledge: he engaged in various acts of worship, had abundant dhikr, built and cared for mosques, and fed the poor. This underscores the Hanafi emphasis on knowledge leading to action (al-‘ilm al-nafi‘). The second part details his travels, particularly to the Hijaz for Hajj and Umrah. In 1280 AH, he taught al-Shifa (a famous work on the Prophet's status) in Medina, indicating his authority in hadith. His meetings with other scholars, such as al-Watari and al-Hadrawi, show his integration into the scholarly network of his time. The journey with Prince Abdul Qadir highlights his social connections. Overall, this biography serves as an introduction to the author's scholarly pedigree and dedication.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): A biographical account of a scholar's life, works, and travels, serving as an introduction to his scholarly authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 1280 AH
C) 1281 AH
D) 1322 AH

Key Takeaway
The tarjama of Shaykh al-Maydani confirms he was a pious, well-connected scholar, making his commentary a trusted source in the Hanafi tradition.

The Scholarly Travels of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical travelogue of the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly connections of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani and explain how his travels contributed to the transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Sheikh al-Maydani's travels linked Damascus, Egypt, and the Hijaz, spreading Hanafi knowledge.

This biographical passage from the introduction to al-Maydani's commentary on al-Quduri traces his journeys and scholarly interactions. While not a fiqh ruling itself, understanding the author's biography helps contextualize his work and the chains of transmission for Hanafi texts. We will explore how his travels reflect the scholarly network of 19th-century Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the destinations
From the passage, list the places al-Maydani visited: Damascus, Egypt, Mecca, Medina. Note the years.
Travels included multiple Hajj trips and a special journey for the Suez Canal opening.
2
Recognize key scholars
Note the scholars he met: Ali al-Watari (Medina), Ahmad al-Hadrawi (Mecca), Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri, and others.
These connections show the breadth of his scholarly network.
3
Analyze the purpose of travel
He traveled for Hajj, to teach, and to attend the Suez Canal opening. The passage suggests reluctance for the latter.
The canal opening was a major international event; his presence was at the prince's insistence.
4
Connect to fiqh transmission
Reflect on how such travels facilitated the spread of texts like 'Al-Shifa' and indirectly supported the Hanafi tradition through the author's commentary on al-Quduri.
Al-Maydani's commentary is a standard Hanafi text; his teachers and students form part of the scholarly chain.
5
Evaluate the author's commentary
The passage does not discuss fiqh directly, but knowing the author's stature adds weight to his commentary. Consider how his life experiences might have influenced his scholarly output.
This step bridges biography to fiqh study.

الجزائري، وذلك لحضور حفل افتتاح قناة السويس،
أقامه الذي
الخديوي إسماعيل، فبقيا في ضيافته سبعة أيام، ثم سافرا إلى الحجاز للحج، ثم عادا إلى دمشق.
وكان افتتاح القناة سنة ١٢٨٦هـ، الموافق ١٨٦٩م، وقد حضر هذا الحفل الضخم الكبير زهاء ستة آلاف من أهل الرفعة والشأن، وكان لهؤلاء الضيوف ثلاث صالات: صالة لعلماء المسلمين، وأخرى للقساوسة ونحوهم من النصارى وصالة ثالثة للحكام والسلاطين في العالم، كإمبراطور فرنسا واليونان وإيطاليا، وغيرها من الدول. وكان ممن سافر من علماء دمشق مع الأمير الجزائري والميداني :

الشريف الشيخ سليم بن نسيب حمزة الحسيني، وغيره.
قلت : من عرف سيرة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، ووقف على طريقة حياته ، عَرَفَ بغلبة الظن أن الشيخ الميداني لـيـس هـو ممـن يرغب في حضور مثل تلك الحفلات، لكن طلـب الأمير الجزائري وإلحاحه عليه، وجبر الميداني لخاطره واستجابة لوجاهته، جعل الميداني يحضر هذا الحفل، ومن هنا تم لقاؤه بعلماء مصر، وعلماء العالم الإسلامي المدعوين مثله لحضور هذا الحفل.

(1) ينظر علماء دمشق وأعيانها في القرن الثالث عشر الهجري ٧٦٨/٣. (۲) تاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر ٢٥/١ ، وينظر تحفة الزائر في مآثر الأمير عبد القادر ۱۲۱/۲ (ذکر توجه الأمير إلى الحجاز).
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. 134. Section Twelve: The Travels of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani made several journeys from Damascus; he traveled to the lands of the Hijaz, Mecca and Medina, multiple times for Hajj and Umrah. One of them was in the year 1280 AH, and during this trip he taught in Medina the book 'Al-Shifa by al-Qadi Iyad' twice, and among those who heard it from him in both sessions was the muhaddith Sheikh Ali ibn Zahir al-Watari al-Madani (1261 AH – 1322 AH), as mentioned by the eminent scholar Sayyid Ja'far ibn Idris al-Kittani (1246 AH – 1323 AH), who narrates 'Al-Shifa' through the chain of al-Watari. In the year 1281 AH, the historian scholar Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi al-Makki met him in Mecca, as he mentioned in his book: Nuzhat al-Fikr. Thus he traveled from Damascus to Egypt, and from there to the Hijaz, and his age at that time was sixty-four years, on a journey with Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri, to attend the opening ceremony of the Suez Canal, which was hosted by Khedive Ismail. They remained his guests for seven days, then traveled to the Hijaz for Hajj, and then returned to Damascus. The opening of the canal was in the year 1286 AH, corresponding to 1869 CE. This huge grand ceremony was attended by nearly six thousand people of high status and importance. The guests had three halls: one hall for Muslim scholars, another for priests and similar Christians, and a third hall for rulers and sultans of the world, such as the Emperor of France, Greece, Italy, and other countries. Among those who traveled from Damascus with Prince al-Jaza'iri and al-Maydani were: the Sharif Sheikh Salim ibn Nasib Hamza al-Husayni, and others. I say: Whoever knows the biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani and is familiar with his way of life will know with strong presumption that Sheikh al-Maydani is not one who desires to attend such gatherings. However, the request of Prince al-Jaza'iri and his insistence, and al-Maydani's wish to please him and respond to his high standing, made al-Maydani attend this ceremony. Hence, he met with scholars of Egypt and scholars of the Islamic world who were also invited to attend this ceremony.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is biographical, providing an account of the travels of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the author of the commentary on al-Quduri. It highlights his scholarly connections, especially in the Hijaz, and his journey to Egypt and the Hijaz in 1286 AH for the opening of the Suez Canal. The author notes that al-Maydani's attendance was reluctant, prompted by the insistence of Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri. This biographical context is important for understanding the author's scholarly stature and his network of teachers and contemporaries.

Key Terms
الوتري (al-Watari): A scholar and muhaddith from Medina, Sheikh Ali ibn Zahir al-Watari, who heard the book 'Al-Shifa' from al-Maydani.
الشفا (al-Shifa): A famous work by al-Qadi Iyad on the virtues and miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), used as a text for teaching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the primary reason al-Maydani traveled to the Suez Canal opening according to the passage?
A) He wanted to meet European rulers
B) He was invited by the Khedive and felt obligated
C) He was pressured by Prince Abd al-Qadir and wanted to please him

Key Takeaway
Knowing the author's biography, including his travels and scholarly connections, deepens the understanding of his fiqh commentary and its place in the Hanafi tradition.

Death of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical account of the author's death and funeral

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount the date, funeral details, and burial location of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani as recorded in Hanafi biographical literature.

Core Idea
Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani passed away on 4 Rabi' al-Awwal 1298 AH, mourned by a large congregation.

This passage from al-Lubab's biography describes the final days and funeral of the great Hanafi scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It provides specific dates, locations, and the public's reverence for his funeral. Understanding these details helps situate his scholarly legacy within Damascus's Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the date of death
Locate the explicit date given in the passage: the 4th of Rabi' al-Awwal, 1298 AH.
This corresponds to 1881 CE; note the error in another source (1274 AH) corrected in the footnote.
2
Locate the funeral prayer specifics
Find the mosque (Jami' al-Daqqaq) and who led the prayer (his son Shaykh Isma'il).
The mosque is also known as Jami' al-Qubaybat in al-Maydan.
3
Describe the burial location
Identify the burial plot (Turbat Bab Allah) and its position (bottom of the middle soil, east side).
Alternative cemetery mentioned by al-Qasimi (al-Qubaybat) but the text affirms Bab Allah.
4
Analyze the poetic eulogy
Read the verses: they praise al-Maydani's virtues and lament the loss of 'the sciences of Abu Hanifa.'
The eulogy highlights his stature as a Hanafi scholar.
5
Reflect on al-Maydani's saying about death
Consider his reported statement expressing contentment with death as meeting the mercy of Allah.
This reflects a pious attitude toward death common among Hanafi scholars.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Section Thirteen
His death, may Allah have mercy on him
(1)
Al-Baytar said in Hilyat al-Bashar: He continued in his uprightness in obedience and worship, and in benefiting his students and visitors, and his kindness to those who sought and desired, until the dove of fate cooed on his tree, and the caller of creatures called him to journey. So he died, may Allah have mercy on him, on the fourth of Rabi' al-Awwal, in the year one thousand two hundred and ninety-eight (1298 AH) (
(2)
(3)
He was prayed over in the Mosque of al-Daqqaq in al-Maydan, led by his virtuous son Shaykh Isma'il, who was brought forward for the imamate by our virtuous teacher al-Tantawi. His funeral procession was witnessed by a crowd that filled the wide road, and he was buried in the soil of: (Bab Allah), at the bottom of the middle soil on the east side(4).

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
137
His son asked me to compose some verses to be written on the grave, so I said: A noble, virtuous, brave, and great imam of lofty stations, he lay in his grave—marvel at a grave that holds a sea whose qualities are lofty. O sorrow, Abd al-Ghani passed quickly, and his companion turned toward the spring of virtue alive in spring with spirit and joy welcoming. One came his date: say, 'The sciences of Abu Hanifa have died.' End. * And it is narrated from Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani that he used to say: When I spend the evening with my pillow of dust and spend the night near the Most Merciful Lord, then congratulate me, my loved ones, and say: Good news to you, you have come to the vast mercy of Allah Almighty, and may He dwell you in His spacious gardens.

I asked
about
this eminent scholar Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id al-Tantawi al-Dimashqi al-Makki, brother of Shaykh Ali al-Tantawi, and he informed me that the Mosque of al-Daqqaq is called the Mosque of al-Qubaybat, and it is in the middle of al-Maydan, this was when I visited him in Makkah al-Mukarramah on Wednesday, 30 Safar 1430 AH. (1) Nahā yanhu means he intended, and in the printed version of 'Ulama Dimashq wa A'yaniha fi al-Qarn al-Thalith 'Ashar al-Hijri 772/2: 'wa najā halifuhu' with a jim. (2) This information was taken from the internet: Hamada and al-Ghanimi), and these two verses are written on the grave of Shaykh al-Maydani, as told to me by the honorable brother Mr. Muhammad Hamada, son of the granddaughter of Shaykh al-Maydani, daughter of the teacher Yusuf ibn Muhammad ibn Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the death of Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of the commentary al-Lubab. It opens with a quote from al-Baytar's Hilyat al-Bashar describing his continued piety and service until his death. The date of death is given as the 4th of Rabi' al-Awwal, 1298 AH (corresponding to 1881 CE). The passage then describes his funeral prayer led by his son Shaykh Isma'il at the Mosque of al-Daqqaq (also known as the Mosque of al-Qubaybat) in the al-Maydan area of Damascus. The funeral was heavily attended. He was buried in a plot called 'Bab Allah' on the east side. A footnote corrects an error in Hadiyyat al-'Arifin which mistakenly recorded his death in 1274 AH. The passage also includes a poetic eulogy composed by someone at the request of his son, praising his virtues and lamenting the loss of the sciences of Abu Hanifa. Finally, it records a saying of al-Maydani that expresses contentment with death as meeting the mercy of Allah, and an editorial note clarifying the location of the mosque.

Key Terms
جامع الدقاق (Jami' al-Daqqaq): The mosque where the funeral prayer was held, located in al-Maydan area of Damascus.
حمام الحمام (Hamam al-Himam): A poetic phrase meaning 'the dove of fate' or 'the dove of death', symbolizing the arrival of death.
تربة باب الله (Turbat Bab Allah): The specific burial plot where al-Maydani was buried, known as 'the soil of the Gate of Allah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what date did Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani pass away?
A) 4th of Rabi' al-Awwal, 1298 AH
B) 12th of Rabi' al-Awwal, 1274 AH
C) 30th of Safar, 1430 AH
D) 4th of Rabi' al-Awwal, 1274 AH

Key Takeaway
Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani died on 4 Rabi' al-Awwal 1298 AH and was buried in Turbat Bab Allah.
